Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Hukm and the Inclusion of Wad'iyyah
Explaining the definition of hukm and the dispute over including ahkam wad'iyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of hukm in Hanafi usul, identify its components, and explain the dispute over including wad'iyyah rulings.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address to the mukallaf by requirement or option; some add wad' to include causes, conditions, and preventers.

After defining fiqh as knowledge of shar'i rulings, it is necessary to define what a hukm is. This lesson unpacks the definition attributed to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, examining how the elements of iqtiḍā' (requirement) and takhyīr (option) generate the six categories of hukm. A key dispute emerges: should the definition explicitly include al-wad' (wad'iyyah rulings) to be comprehensive? The passage presents both sides of this usul debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genus and differentia in the definition
The definition 'the address of Allah related to the acts of the mukallafin by way of requirement or option' contains a genus (address of Allah) and two differentiae: 'related to the acts of the mukallafin' and 'by requirement or option'. Understand how each component functions to include or exclude certain addresses.
The first differentia excludes addresses about divine attributes or stories; the second excludes informative statements like 'Allah created you'.
2
Derive the six categories from iqtiḍā' and takhyīr
Iqtiḍā' (requirement) splits into request to do and request to refrain. Each can be decisive or non-decisive, yielding wajib, nadb, haram, makruh tahrimi, and makruh tanzihi. Takhyīr gives ibahah. Trace how these six encompass all taklifi rulings.
Note that the Hanafi school counts five or six: the text explicitly adds makruh tanzihi as a sixth.
3
Understand the objection leading to the addition of 'aw al-wad''
The objection: the definition without 'aw al-wad'' covers only taklifi rulings, not wad'iyyah (cause, condition, preventer). Examine why wad'i rulings like 'the sun's declining is a cause for prayer' do not contain an explicit request, so they seem excluded.
Wad'i rulings are still shar'i rulings; the question is whether the definition must explicitly mention them.
4
Compare the two positions on including al-wad'
Some scholars add 'aw al-wad'' to make the definition comprehensive. Others omit it, arguing that iqtiḍā' can be implicit: wad'i rulings indirectly imply a requirement (e.g., the cause implicitly commands the act). Evaluate the strengths of each position.
The text presents both without giving a clear tarjih, reflecting a legitimate ikhtilaf.

ولما عرف الفقه بالعلم بالاحكام الشرعية وجب تعريف الحكم وتعريف الشرعية فقال والحكم قيل خطاب اللہ تعالی مصنف اپنی عبارت تنقیح کو ماقبل سے ربط دے رہے ہیں کہ جب ہم نے متن تنقیح میں فقہ کی تعریف ھوا العلم بالاحکام الشرعیہ سے کی تو ہمارے اوپر واجب ہے کہ حکم کی تعریف کریں اور الشرعیہ کی بھی تعریف بیان کریں اس لیے ہم حکم کی تعریف کرتے ہیں بعض حضرات نے حکم کی تعریف کی ہے خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخيير مصنف نے وضاحت فرمائی کہ یہ تعریف امام ابوالحسن اشعری سے منقول ہے فقولہ خطاب اللہ سے فوائد قیود بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ تعریف حکم میں خطاب اللہ درجہ جنس ہے جمیع خطابات اللہ کو بلا تقیید تخصیص شامل ہے اور المتعلق با فعال المکلفین فصل اول ہے اس سے وہ خطابات اللہ خارج ہو گئے جو افعال واعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں جیسے قص و امثال وہ آیات جو صفات اللہ کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں جیسے لا اله الا اللہ وغیرہ البتہ والله خلقكم وما تعملون جیسا خطاب افعال المتکلفین میں داخل ہو کر حکم کی تعریف میں باقی ہے آیت کا معنی یہ ہے کہ

اللہ تعالی تمہارا بھی خالق ہے اور تمہارے اعمال کا بھی تو یہ بھی خطاب اللہ متعلق بہ اعمال مکلفین ہے حالانکہ اس کو فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں حکم نہیں کہا جاتا اس لیے اس کے اخراج کیلئے قید مزید کی ضرورت تھی تو بالاقتضا او التخییر کی قید لگا کرو الله خلقكم وما تعملون ونجود کو خارج کر دیا گیا کیونکہ اقتضاء بمعنی طلب ہے اور والله خلقكم وما تعملون میں طلب فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں صرف خبر ہے کہ تمہارا اور تمہارے اعمال کا خالق اللہ ہے۔ وهو اما طلب الفعل سے مصنف یہ بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ بالاقتضاء او التخيیر میں حکم کی تمام اقسام داخل ہو گئیں کیونکہ الاقتضاء بمعنی طلب ہے پھر طلب میں تعمیم ہے خواہ طلب فعل ہو خواہ طلب ترک ہوا اگر طلب فعل ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں طلب جازم ہوگی ( منع عن الترک ہوگا ) یا طلب غیر جازم ( مع عدم منع الترک ) اول واجب ، دوم ندب، اگر طلب ترک ہو تو دوصورتیں ہیں طلب ترک جازم ہوگا یا غیر جازم اول حرام دوم مکروہ تحریمی و تنزیہی او اتخمیر میں اباحت آگئی تو حکم کی چھا اقسام آ گئیں۔
وقد زاد البعض او الوضع الخ مصنف یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بعض حضرات نے تعریف حکم میں اوالوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کیا ہے ای بالاقتضاء او التخيير او الوضع ، اب سوال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ ان حضرات نے اوا لوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کیوں کیا تو مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ان حضرات نے ایک اشکال سے بچنے کیلئے اس قید کا اضافہ کیا اشکال کی تقریر یہ ہے علم بمعنی خطاب اللہ کی دوقسمیں ہیں (۱) علم تکلیفی (۲) کم وضعی حکم تکلیفی ، وہ ہے جس میں مکلفین کو افعال و اعمال کی تکلیف دی گئی ہو کما مر سابقا (۲) حکم وضعی وہ ہے جس میں یہ بیان کیا گیا کہ فلان چیز فلاں کیلئے سبب ہے جیسے دلوک شمس سبب صلوۃ ہے یا آمیں یہ بیان کیا گیا ہو کہ فلاں شئی فلاں کیلئے شرط ہے جیسے طہارت شرط صلوۃ ہے یا یہ بیان کیا جائے کہ فلان شئی فلان کیلئے مانع ہے جیسے النجاسة في بدن المصلى مانعة عن الصلوة ونحوهما سے یہی مانعیت مراد ہے خلاصہ ایں کہ حکم وضعی میں سبیت مسیبیت شرطیة ومشروطیة ومانعیت کا بیان ہوتا ہے اس میں کسی فعل کا طلب نہیں ہوتا اب اشکال یہ ہوتا تھا کہ اگر حکم کی تعریف میں صرف بالاقتضاء اوالخیر پر اکتفاء کیا جائے اورا وضع کی قید نہ لگائی جائے تو تعریف حکم اپنی دو قسموں میں سے ایک (یعنی خطاب تکلیفی ) کو تو شامل ہوگی لیکن خطاب وضعی کو شامل نہیں ہوگی تو تعریف حکم جامع نہیں رہے گی اسی اشکال (غیر جامعیت تعریف حکم ) سے بچنے کیلئے بعض حضرات نے تعریف حکم میں ادا الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کیا تا کہ تعریف حکم اپنی دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہو کر جامع بن جائے و البعض لم يذكر الوضعی، اور بعض حضرات او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ نہیں کرتے اب ان پر اشکال ہوا کہ پھر تو حکم کی تعریف جامع نہ رہی صرف علم تکلیفی پر صادق آ رہی ہے حکم وضعی پر صادق نہیں آرہی تو وہ جواب دیتے ہیں کہ حکم کی تعریف جامع ہے دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہے الاقتضاء میں حکم وضعی بھی داخل ہے کیونکہ الاقتضاء کی دو قسمیں ہیں کبھی اقتضاء مضر یکی ہوتا ہے اور کبھی ضمنی حکم وضعی میں اگر چہ صراحت اقتضاء نہیں ہوتا لیکن ضمنا اس میں بھی اقتضا فعل ہوتا ہے
Matn al-Tawdih: 'And when fiqh was defined as knowledge of the shar'i rulings, it became necessary to define al-hukm and al-shar'iyyah. So he said: al-hukm is said to be the address of Allah.' The author connects his words in Tanqih to what precedes: When we defined fiqh in the matn of Tanqih as knowledge of the shar'i rulings, it became obligatory upon us to define al-hukm and also to explain the meaning of al-shar'iyyah. Therefore, we define al-hukm. Some scholars have defined al-hukm as 'the address of Allah, the Exalted, related to the acts of the mukallafin by way of requirement (iqtiḍā') or option (takhayyur).' The author clarifies that this definition is transmitted from Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. By his saying 'the address of Allah,' he explains the benefits of the restrictions: In the definition of hukm, 'address of Allah' is the genus, including all addresses of Allah without restriction or specification. 'Related to the acts of the mukallafin' is the first differentia. It excludes those addresses of Allah that are not related to the acts of the mukallafin, such as stories and parables, and those verses that relate to the attributes of Allah, such as 'La ilaha illa Allah.' However, something like 'And Allah created you and what you do' is included in the address related to the acts of the mukallafin and remains in the definition of hukm. The meaning of the verse is that Allah is the Creator of you and your deeds. So this also is an address of Allah related to the acts of the mukallafin, but it is not called a hukm in the terminology of the fuqaha'. Therefore, to exclude it, an additional restriction was needed. So the restriction 'by requirement or option' was added to exclude 'And Allah created you and what you do' because iqtiḍā' means request, and in 'And Allah created you and what you do' there is no request for action; rather, it is merely information that Allah is the Creator of you and your deeds. 'And it is either a request for an action'—the author states that by 'by requirement or option' all categories of hukm are included, because iqtiḍā' means request, and request includes both request to do and request to refrain. If it is a request to do, there are two forms: a decisive request (which prohibits omission) or a non-decisive request (without prohibiting omission). The first is wajib, the second is nadb. If it is a request to refrain, there are two forms: a decisive request to refrain or a non-decisive one. The first is haram, the second is makruh tahrimi or tanzihi. And takhyir includes ibahah. Thus, six categories of hukm are covered. 'And some added 'or al-wad''—the author says that some scholars added the restriction 'or al-wad'' to the definition of hukm, i.e., 'by requirement or option or al-wad''. Now the question arises: why did these scholars add this restriction? The author answers that they added it to avoid an objection. The exposition of the objection: Knowledge, meaning the address of Allah, is of two types: (1) taklifi hukm and (2) wad'i hukm. Taklifi hukm is that in which the mukallafin are charged with acts, as mentioned earlier. (2) Wad'i hukm is that in which it is stated that such-and-such a thing is a cause for such-and-such, like the declining of the sun is a cause for prayer; or it is stated that such-and-such a thing is a condition for such-and-such, like purity is a condition for prayer; or it is stated that such-and-such a thing is a preventer for such-and-such, like impurity on the body of the one praying is a preventer for prayer. The bottom line is that the wad'i hukm involves the statement of causality, conditionality, and prevention. There is no request for any action in it. Now the objection was: if the definition of hukm is restricted to 'by requirement or option' and the restriction 'or al-wad'' is not added, then the definition would include only one of its two types (i.e., taklifi address) but would not include wad'i address. Thus, the definition would not be comprehensive. To avoid this objection (lack of comprehensiveness), some scholars added the restriction 'or al-wad'' so that the definition of hukm would include both types and become comprehensive. 'And some did not mention al-wad''—and some scholars do not add the restriction 'or al-wad''. Then they are faced with the objection that the definition is no longer comprehensive; it only applies to taklifi hukm and does not apply to wad'i hukm. They respond that the definition of hukm is comprehensive and includes both types because iqtiḍā' is of two types: sometimes iqtiḍā' is explicit and sometimes implicit. In wad'i hukm, although there is no explicit iqtiḍā', it implicitly contains iqtiḍā' of action.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the definition of 'hukm' (divine ruling) in usul al-fiqh, following the matn of al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shari'ah. The author explains that after defining fiqh as knowledge of the shar'i rulings, it is necessary to define what a hukm is and what 'shar'i' means. The definition attributed to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari is: 'The address of Allah, the Exalted, related to the acts of the mukallafin by way of requirement (iqtiḍā') or option (takhayyur).' The author breaks down the definition: 'address of Allah' is the genus covering all divine addresses; 'related to the acts of the mukallafin' excludes addresses about stories, attributes, etc. However, a verse like 'And Allah created you and what you do' (Quran 37:96) is about acts of the mukallafin but does not constitute a hukm because it is merely informative, not a request. So the phrase 'by requirement or option' is added to exclude such informative statements. Then the author shows how this definition covers the five categories (wajib, haram, mandub, makruh, mubah) and adds a sixth (makruh tanzihi) by splitting the request to act and refrain into decisive and non-decisive. The main dispute arises regarding the inclusion of 'al-wad'' (the wad'iyyah rulings, i.e., cause, condition, preventer). Some scholars add 'or al-wad'' to the definition to make it comprehensive of both taklifi and wad'i rulings. The author presents the argument: without 'al-wad'', the definition only covers taklifi rulings. Those who exclude 'al-wad'' argue that iqtiḍā' (requirement) is broad enough to include implicit requirement in wad'i rulings (e.g., the sun's declining implicitly requires prayer). The author does not explicitly take sides but presents both views. This reflects the Hanafi usul discourse on the scope of hukm.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The address of Allah related to the acts of the mukallafin by way of requirement (iqtiḍā') or option (takhayyur), and some include wad'iyyah.
اقتضاء (iqtiḍā'): Requirement or demand; includes both request to do and request to refrain.
تخییر (takhayyur): Option; the category of ibahah (permissibility).
وضع (wad'): The category of hukm wad'i: cause, condition, preventer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do some scholars add the restriction 'aw al-wad'' to the definition of hukm?
A) To exclude informative verses like 'Allah created you'.
B) To make the definition comprehensive of both taklifi and wad'i rulings.
C) To include the six categories of hukm.
D) To emphasize that hukm requires request.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm in Hanafi usul centers on iqtiḍā' and takhyīr, with a debate over the explicit inclusion of wad'iyyah, reflecting the scope of divine address.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Defining Hukm: The Case for Including Wad'i Rulings
Arguing that the definition of hukm must include declaratory rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two competing definitions of hukm shari, explain why some scholars add 'aw al-wad'', and evaluate the author's preferred position using the distinction between taklifi and wad'i concepts.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm must explicitly include declaratory rulings; demand alone is insufficient.

This passage from the Sharh on Al-Tawdih tackles a foundational usul issue: what exactly is a hukm shari? The standard definition using 'bi al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' covers the five taklifi rulings, but it excludes the wad'i rulings that establish causes, conditions, and preventers. Some scholars argue these are implicitly included, but the author insists they must be stated explicitly to make the definition comprehensive (jami'). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and helps you see why precise definitional boundaries matter for legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of khitab (taklifi and wad'i)
Distinguish between discourse that directly demands or permits action (taklifi) and discourse that merely declares something to be a cause, condition, or preventer (wad'i). The example given is 'Allah created you and your actions' – it is informative, not demanding, so it is excluded from taklifi hukm.
Wad'i rulings include sabab (cause), shart (condition), and mani‘ (preventer).
2
Understand the objection to the incomplete definition
If the definition only says 'bi al-iqtida’ aw al-takhyir', it only covers taklifi rulings. Wad'i rulings would be left out, making the definition non-comprehensive. Hence some scholars added 'aw al-wad''.
Comprehensiveness (jami‘) is a key requirement for a definition.
3
Analyze the counterargument that wad'i is implicit in iqtida'
Proponents of the simpler definition argue that wad'i rulings imply a demand. For example, 'The decline of the sun is a cause for prayer' implicitly demands prayer when the cause occurs. Thus iqtida' covers wad'i implicitly.
Implicit demand (iqtida' dimni) is the basis of this argument.
4
Evaluate the author's tarjih based on conceptual distinction
The author rejects the implicit inclusion because taklifi and wad'i are conceptually distinct (mutabayin). Taklifi is about demand; wad'i is about relational facts. Even if they often entail each other, they are not the same. Therefore the definition must mention both explicitly.
The author sides with the first group: the definition should include 'aw al-wad''.

اللہ تعالی تمہارا بھی خالق ہے اور تمہارے اعمال کا بھی تو یہ بھی خطاب اللہ متعلق بہ اعمال مکلفین ہے حالانکہ اس کو فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں حکم نہیں کہا جاتا اس لیے اس کے اخراج کیلئے قید مزید کی ضرورت تھی تو بالاقتضا او التخییر کی قید لگا کرو الله خلقكم وما تعملون ونجود کو خارج کر دیا گیا کیونکہ اقتضاء بمعنی طلب ہے اور والله خلقكم وما تعملون میں طلب فعل نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں صرف خبر ہے کہ تمہارا اور تمہارے اعمال کا خالق اللہ ہے۔ وهو اما طلب الفعل سے مصنف یہ بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ بالاقتضاء او التخییر میں حکم کی تمام اقسام داخل ہو گئیں کیونکہ الاقتضاء بمعنی طلب ہے پھر طلب میں تعمیم ہے خواہ طلب فعل ہو خواہ طلب ترک ہوا اگر طلب فعل ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں طلب جازم ہوگی ( منع عن الترک ہوگا ) یا طلب غیر جازم ( مع عدم منع الترک ) اول واجب ، دوم ندب، اگر طلب ترک ہو تو دوصورتیں ہیں طلب ترک جازم ہوگا یا غیر جازم اول حرام دوم مکروہ تحریمی و تنزیہی او اتخمیر میں اباحت آگئی تو حکم کی چھا اقسام آ گئیں۔
وقد زاد البعض او الوضع الخ مصنف یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بعض حضرات نے تعریف حکم میں اوالوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کیا ہے ای بالاقتضاء او التخيير او الوضع ، اب سوال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ ان حضرات نے اوا لوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کیوں کیا تو مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ان حضرات نے ایک اشکال سے بچنے کیلئے اس قید کا اضافہ کیا اشکال کی تقریر یہ ہے علم بمعنی خطاب اللہ کی دوقسمیں ہیں (۱) علم تکلیفی (۲) کم وضعی حکم تکلیفی ، وہ ہے جس میں مکلفین کو افعال و اعمال کی تکلیف دی گئی ہو کما مر سابقا (۲) حکم وضعی وہ ہے جس میں یہ بیان کیا گیا کہ فلان چیز فلاں کیلئے سبب ہے جیسے دلوک شمس سبب صلوۃ ہے یا آمیں یہ بیان کیا گیا ہو کہ فلاں شئی فلاں کیلئے شرط ہے جیسے طہارت شرط صلوۃ ہے یا یہ بیان کیا جائے کہ فلان شئی فلان کیلئے مانع ہے جیسے النجاسة في بدن المصلى مانعة عن الصلوة ونحوهما سے یہی مانعیت مراد ہے خلاصہ ایں کہ حکم وضعی میں سبیت مسیبیت شرطیة ومشروطیة ومانعیت کا بیان ہوتا ہے اس میں کسی فعل کا طلب نہیں ہوتا اب اشکال یہ ہوتا تھا کہ اگر حکم کی تعریف میں صرف بالاقتضاء اوالخیر پر اکتفاء کیا جائے اورا وضع کی قید نہ لگائی جائے تو تعریف حکم اپنی دو قسموں میں سے ایک (یعنی خطاب تکلیفی ) کو تو شامل ہوگی لیکن خطاب وضعی کو شامل نہیں ہوگی تو تعریف حکم جامع نہیں رہے گی اسی اشکال (غیر جامعیت تعریف حکم ) سے بچنے کیلئے بعض حضرات نے تعریف حکم میں ادا الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کیا تا کہ تعریف حکم اپنی دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہو کر جامع بن جائے و البعض لم يذكر الوضعی، اور بعض حضرات او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ نہیں کرتے اب ان پر اشکال ہوا کہ پھر تو حکم کی تعریف جامع نہ رہی صرف علم تکلیفی پر صادق آ رہی ہے حکم وضعی پر صادق نہیں آرہی تو وہ جواب دیتے ہیں کہ حکم کی تعریف جامع ہے دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہے الاقتضاء میں حکم وضعی بھی داخل ہے کیونکہ الاقتضاء کی دو قسمیں ہیں کبھی اقتضاء مضر یکی ہوتا ہے اور کبھی ضمنی حکم وضعی میں اگر چہ صراحت اقتضاء نہیں ہوتا لیکن ضمنا اس میں بھی اقتضا فعل ہوتا ہے
مثلا دلوک شمس سبب صلوۃ ہے تو بظاہر اس میں سبیت کا بیان ہے لیکن ضمنا اس میں اقتضاء فعل ہے اس کا معنی یہ ہوگا کہ جب دلوک شمس پایا جائے تو نماز واجب ہے وجوب فعل من باب الاقتضاء ہے لہذا حکم وضعی الاقتضاء میں داخل ہو گیا اور حکم کی تعریف اپنی دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہو کر جامع ہوگئی اس لیۓ اوالوضع کی قید کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ لکن الحق ھو الاول سے مصنف اپنی رائے بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ میرے نزدیک حق بات یہ ہے کہ حکم کی تعریف میں اوالوضع کی قید ہونی چاہئے تاکہ تعریف دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہو جائے باقی رہی دوسرے حضرات کی دلیل کہ حکم وضعی الاقتضاء میں داخل ہے تو مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں حکم وضعی کو الاقتضاء میں داخل کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ دونوں مفہوم و حقیقت کے اعتبار سے ایک دوسرے کی متفاسیر ومتباین ہیں کیونکہ تکلیفی کا مفہوم خطاب الله المتعلق الخ، اور حکم وضعی کا مفہوم تعلق کئی بشئ آخر ہے لہذا ایک کو دوسرے میں داخل کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے بلکہ ہر ایک کو مستقلا ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے البتہ بعض صورتوں میں یہ دونوں ایک دوسرے کو لازم ملزوم ہوتے ہیں ایک حکم مستلزم ہوتا ہے دوسرے کو مثلا دلوک شمس کی سبیت مستلزم ہے وجوب صلوۃ کو لیکن اس سے یہ تو لازم نہیں آتا کہ یہ دونوں متحد ہو جائیں اتحاد اور ہوتا ہے استلزام اور ہوتا ہے لہذا مصنف نے مذہب اول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے۔ وبعضهم قد عرف الحكم الشرعي بهذا اى بعض المتاخرین ، پہلے تو مصنف نے یہ بیان کیا تھا کہ بعض اشاعرہ مطلق حکم ( حکم بسیط ) جس میں شرعی کی قید نہیں ہے اس کی تعریف خطاب اللہ تعالی الخ کے ساتھ کرتے ہیں اب یہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ بعض متاخرین اشاعرہ حکم مطلق کی یہ تعریف نہیں کرتے بلکہ حکم شرعی ( حکم ہو اور ہو بھی شرعی ) یعنی حکم مقید بقید الشرعی کی تعریف خطاب الخ کے ساتھ کرتے ہیں لہذا اس صورت میں مطلق حکم کی تعریف خطاب اللہ تعالی نہیں ہوگی بلکہ حکم مطلق کی تعریف اسناد امرالی امر آخر ہوگی ۔ والفقهاء يطلقونه على ماثبت بالخطاب الخ تعریف سابق تو عند الاصولین تھی اب مصنف فقہاء کی تعریف بیان کر رہے ہیں عند الفقہا حکم کی تعریف ہے ما ثبت بالخطاب وہ چیز جو خطاب سے ثابت ہو مثلا اقیموا الصلوۃ اس سے وجوب صلوۃ ثابت ہو رہا ہے تو وجوب کو حکم کہا جائے گا :سوال، معنی فقہاء اور معنی اصولیین میں فرق کیا ہے۔ جواب: فرق واضح ہے کہ معنی اصولیین خطاب اللہ ہے اور خطاب اللہ من صفات اللہ ہے تو دریں صورت حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ ہو کر صفتہ اللہ ہوگا اور حکم بمعنی ما ثبت بالخطاب یہ فعل مکلف کی صفت ہے تو خلاصہ فرق یہ ہے کہ حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ صفہ اللہ ہے اور حکم بمعنی ما ثبت بالخطاب صفة فعل خلق اللہ ہے۔ بطریق اطلاق المصدر جواب سوال مقدر ۔ سوال ! یہ ہے کہ حکم مصدر ہے لہذا اس کا معنی ما ثبت بالخطاب درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ما ثبت بالخطاب معنی مصدری نہیں ہے بلکہ حاصل بالمصدر ہے حالانکہ مصدر کا معنی بھی مصدری ہونا چاہئے ۔ جواب ! مصنف خود جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ حقیقہ تو حکم مصدر ہے لیکن یہاں مصدر کو منی لمفعول (اسم مفعول) کے معنی میں نقل کیا گیا مجازا تو حکم بمعنی ما حکم
(The author discusses the definition of hukm shari.) Allah is the Creator of you and your actions; this is also Allah's discourse related to the actions of the legally responsible, yet it is not called hukm in the terminology of jurists. Therefore, an additional qualifier was needed to exclude it, so the qualifier 'by requirement or choice' was added to exclude 'Allah created you and what you do' because requirement means demand, and 'Allah created you and what you do' does not contain a demand of action but rather information that Allah is the Creator of you and your actions. Then (the author says) through 'or demand of action' he states that all types of hukm are included in 'by requirement or choice' because al-iqtida' means demand; then demand is general, whether demand of action or demand of omission. If demand of action, there are two forms: decisive demand (forbidding omission) or non-decisive demand (without forbidding omission); first is wajib, second is nadb. If demand of omission, there are two forms: decisive demand of omission or non-decisive; first is haram, second is makruh tahrimi and tanzihi. And 'or choice' includes ibaha. Thus the six types of hukm are included. 
'And some added 'or al-wad''. The author says that some scholars added the qualifier 'or al-wad'' to the definition of hukm, i.e., 'by requirement or choice or declaratory'. Now the question arises: why did they add this qualifier? The author answers that they added this qualifier to avoid an objection. The objection is as follows: Knowledge in the sense of Allah's discourse has two types: (1) taklifi discourse; (2) wad'i discourse. Taklifi hukm is that in which the legally responsible are charged with actions, as before. (2) Wad'i hukm is that in which it is stated that something is a cause for something else, like the decline of the sun is a cause for prayer; or something is a condition, like purity is a condition for prayer; or something is a preventer, like impurity on the body of the worshiper prevents prayer, etc. In summary, wad'i hukm expresses causality, conditionedness, and prevenience. It does not involve demand of action. Now the objection was: if the definition of hukm is restricted to 'by requirement or choice' without adding 'or declaratory', then the definition would include only one of its two types (taklifi discourse) but not wad'i discourse, so the definition would not be comprehensive. To avoid this objection (of non-comprehensiveness), some added the qualifier 'or al-wad'' so that the definition of hukm includes both types and becomes comprehensive. And some did not mention 'al-wad''. Now the objection against them is that then the definition is not comprehensive; it applies only to taklifi discourse and not to wad'i. They reply that the definition of hukm is comprehensive and includes both types because wad'i hukm is also included in al-iqtida' since al-iqtida' has two forms: sometimes iqtida' is explicit, sometimes implicit. In wad'i hukm, although explicit iqtida' is not present, implicitly there is a demand of action. For example, the decline of the sun is a cause for prayer. Apparently it is a statement of causality, but implicitly it contains a demand of action; its meaning is: when the decline of the sun occurs, prayer is obligatory. The obligation of action is from the angle of iqtida'. Therefore, wad'i hukm is included in iqtida', and the definition becomes comprehensive, so there is no need for the qualifier 'or al-wad''. 'But the truth is the first'—the author expresses his opinion: in my view the truth is that the definition of hukm should include 'or al-wad'' so that the definition includes both types. As for the other scholars' argument that wad'i hukm is included in iqtida', the author replies: it is incorrect to include wad'i hukm in iqtida' because both are mutually exclusive and different in concept and reality. The concept of taklifi is 'Allah's discourse related...' and the concept of wad'i is 'relation of something to another thing'. Therefore, including one in the other is not correct; rather, each must be mentioned independently. However, in some cases they are necessary concomitants; one entails the other, e.g., the causality of the decline of the sun entails the obligation of prayer. But this does not require that they become one; unification is one thing, entailment is another. Hence the author considers the first opinion preponderant. 'And some have defined shari hukm by this' i.e., some later scholars. Earlier the author said that some Ash'aris define absolute hukm (simple hukm, not qualified by shari) as 'Allah's discourse...'. Now he says that some later Ash'aris do not define absolute hukm this way; rather they define shari hukm (hukm qualified by shari) as 'discourse...'. So in this case, absolute hukm is not defined as Allah's discourse, but rather as the attribution of one thing to another. 'And the jurists apply it to what is established by discourse'—the previous definition was from the usuliyun; now the author states the definition of the fuqaha: according to the fuqaha, hukm is 'what is established by discourse', e.g., 'Establish prayer' establishes the obligation of prayer, so obligation is called hukm. Question: What is the difference between the meaning of the fuqaha and the meaning of the usuliyun? Answer: The difference is clear: the meaning of the usuliyun is Allah's discourse, and Allah's discourse is an attribute of Allah; thus hukm in the sense of Allah's discourse becomes an attribute of Allah. And hukm in the sense of 'what is established by discourse' is an attribute of the action of the legally responsible. So the summary is: hukm in the sense of Allah's discourse is an attribute of Allah, and hukm in the sense of 'what is established by discourse' is an attribute of the action of Allah's creation. By transitive use of the verbal noun—answering a presumed question. Question: Hukm is a verbal noun; therefore its meaning as 'what is established by discourse' is not correct because 'what is established by discourse' is not the verbal noun meaning but the object of the verbal noun, whereas the meaning of the verbal noun should be the verbal noun itself. Answer: The author himself replies: in reality, hukm is a verbal noun, but here the verbal noun has been transferred metaphorically to the meaning of the passive participle; thus hukm means 'what is ruled'.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion from the Sharh on Al-Tawdih regarding the definition of hukm shari (Islamic legal ruling). The author begins by explaining that the qualifier 'bi al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' (by requirement or choice) is necessary to exclude mere informative statements about Allah's creation, which are not hukm in the fiqh sense. He then enumerates the six types of hukm that are included under iqtida' (demand) and takhyir (choice): wajib, mandub, haram, makruh (both tahrimi and tanzihi), and mubah. 

He then presents the disagreement among scholars: some added the qualifier 'aw al-wad'' (or declaratory ruling) to the definition to ensure it covers both taklifi (obligatory) and wad'i (declaratory) rulings. The objection is that without this addition, the definition would be incomplete because it would only cover taklifi rulings. The defenders of the original definition argue that wad'i rulings are implicitly included because they entail a demand (iqtida') — for example, stating that the decline of the sun is a cause for prayer implies that prayer is obligatory when that cause occurs. 

The author (possibly Sadr al-Shariah or the commentator) rejects this reasoning, asserting that taklifi and wad'i rulings are distinct in concept and reality; one cannot be subsumed under the other merely because they are sometimes related. He prefers the first opinion that explicitly includes 'aw al-wad''. 

Finally, the passage discusses a terminological difference: the usuliyun (scholars of usul) define hukm as Allah's discourse (an attribute of Allah), while the fuqaha (jurists) define it as what is established by that discourse (an attribute of the action). The author addresses a possible objection regarding the use of the verbal noun 'hukm' to mean the passive participle, explaining that it is a metaphorical transfer (naql majazi). 

Throughout, the commentary maintains a rigorous distinction between the two senses of hukm and the necessity of a comprehensive definition.

Key Terms
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Demand or requirement, including both demand of action and demand of omission.
التخيير (al-takhyir): Choice, indicating permissibility (ibaha).
الحكم الوضعي (al-hukm al-wad'i): Declaratory ruling that establishes something as a cause, condition, or preventer without demanding action directly.
باب المصدر (bab al-masdar): The verbal noun used in its original form meaning the action itself, but here metaphorically transferred to the meaning of the passive participle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's preferred opinion, why must the definition of hukm include 'aw al-wad''?
A) Because wad'i rulings are more important than taklifi rulings
B) Because without it, the definition would only cover taklifi rulings, leaving out wad'i rulings, making it non-comprehensive
C) Because the fuqaha define hukm as what is established by discourse
D) Because the Ash'aris defined hukm as Allah's discourse

Key Takeaway
The author holds that the definition of hukm must explicitly include wad'i rulings to be comprehensive because taklifi and wad'i are conceptually distinct, even though they can entail each other.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
The Definition of Hukm: Necessity of 'Al-Wad'i' and Fuqaha Usage
Explaining the definition of hukm, necessity of al-wad'i qayd, and distinction between usuliyyun and fuqaha definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi definition of hukm from the usuliyyun definition, explain why the qualifier 'al-wad'i' is necessary, and apply the distinction between taklifi and wad'i rulings.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of hukm explicitly includes both taklifi and wad'i because they are distinct in meaning and reality.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the precise definition of 'hukm' is a foundational issue. This passage clarifies why the Hanafi school insists on including the qualifier 'al-wad'i' in the definition, and contrasts the usuliyyun definition (hukm as divine address) with the fuqaha definition (hukm as the result of that address). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly analyzing legal rulings and their components.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main definitions of hukm
Locate in the passage where the definition according to usuliyyun (khitab Allah) and according to fuqaha (ma thabata bil-khitab) are stated. Note the difference in what is being defined: the address itself vs. the established ruling.
The usuliyyun definition treats hukm as an attribute of Allah; the fuqaha treat it as an attribute of the mukallaf's act.
2
Analyze the dispute over including 'al-wad'i'
Examine the objection: some scholars argue that the definition of hukm does not need 'al-wad'i' because wad'i rulings (like sabab) are implicitly included in the implication (iqtida) of taklifi rulings. Identify their example (zawal as sabab for prayer).
Their reasoning is that if wad'i implies taklifi, then mentioning both separately is redundant.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
See how the author (commentator) rejects this, arguing that taklifi and wad'i are distinct in meaning and reality. They may be mutually entailing (lazim malzum) but not identical. Therefore the definition must explicitly mention both.
Key distinction: ittihad (union) vs. iltizam (entailment).
4
Differentiate the definitions of usuliyyun and fuqaha
Note that for usuliyyun, hukm = khitab Allah (divine address) – this is an attribute of Allah. For fuqaha, hukm = ma thabata bil-khitab (what is established by the address) – this is an attribute of the mukallaf's act. This resolves apparent contradictions when reading usul vs. fiqh texts.
The fuqaha definition involves a metaphorical transfer (naql majazi) from masdar to ism maf'ul, which became a technical reality (haqiqa istilahiyya).
5
Apply the distinction to practical analysis
When encountering a ruling, determine whether it is being discussed as a divine address (usuli sense) or as the resulting obligation/prohibition/etc. (fiqh sense). This prevents confusion in understanding proofs and obligations.
e.g., 'Establish prayer' – the divine address is the command (usuli hukm), the obligation established is the fiqhi hukm.

مثلا دلوک شمس سبب صلوۃ ہے تو بظاہر اس میں سبیت کا بیان ہے لیکن ضمنا اس میں اقتضاء فعل ہے اس کا معنی یہ ہوگا کہ جب دلوک شمس پایا جائے تو نماز واجب ہے وجوب فعل من باب الاقتضاء ہے لہذا حکم وضعی الاقتضاء میں داخل ہو گیا اور حکم کی تعریف اپنی دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہو کر جامع ہوگئی اس لیۓ اوالوضع کی قید کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ لکن الحق ھو الاول سے مصنف اپنی رائے بیان فرما رہے ہیں کہ میرے نزدیک حق بات یہ ہے کہ حکم کی تعریف میں اوالوضع کی قید ہونی چاہئے تاکہ تعریف دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہو جائے باقی رہی دوسرے حضرات کی دلیل کہ حکم وضعی الاقتضاء میں داخل ہے تو مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں حکم وضعی کو الاقتضاء میں داخل کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ دونوں مفہوم و حقیقت کے اعتبار سے ایک دوسرے کی متفاسیر ومتباین ہیں کیونکہ تکلیفی کا مفہوم خطاب الله المتعلق الخ، اور حکم وضعی کا مفہوم تعلق کئی بشئ آخر ہے لہذا ایک کو دوسرے میں داخل کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے بلکہ ہر ایک کو مستقلا ذکر کرنا ضروری ہے البتہ بعض صورتوں میں یہ دونوں ایک دوسرے کو لازم ملزوم ہوتے ہیں ایک حکم مستلزم ہوتا ہے دوسرے کو مثلا دلوک شمس کی سبیت مستلزم ہے وجوب صلوۃ کو لیکن اس سے یہ تو لازم نہیں آتا کہ یہ دونوں متحد ہو جائیں اتحاد اور ہوتا ہے استلزام اور ہوتا ہے لہذا مصنف نے مذہب اول کو راجح قرار دیا ہے۔ وبعضهم قد عرف الحكم الشرعي بهذا اى بعض المتاخرین ، پہلے تو مصنف نے یہ بیان کیا تھا کہ بعض اشاعرہ مطلق حکم ( حکم بسیط ) جس میں شرعی کی قید نہیں ہے اس کی تعریف خطاب اللہ تعالی الخ کے ساتھ کرتے ہیں اب یہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ بعض متاخرین اشاعرہ حکم مطلق کی یہ تعریف نہیں کرتے بلکہ حکم شرعی ( حکم ہو اور ہو بھی شرعی ) یعنی حکم مقید بقید الشرعی کی تعریف خطاب الخ کے ساتھ کرتے ہیں لہذا اس صورت میں مطلق حکم کی تعریف خطاب اللہ تعالی نہیں ہوگی بلکہ حکم مطلق کی تعریف اسناد امرالی امر آخر ہوگی ۔ والفقهاء يطلقونه على ماثبت بالخطاب الخ تعریف سابق تو عند الاصولین تھی اب مصنف فقہاء کی تعریف بیان کر رہے ہیں عند الفقہا حکم کی تعریف ہے ما ثبت بالخطاب وہ چیز جو خطاب سے ثابت ہو مثلا اقیموا الصلوۃ اس سے وجوب صلوۃ ثابت ہو رہا ہے تو وجوب کو حکم کہا جائے گا :سوال، معنی فقہاء اور معنی اصولیین میں فرق کیا ہے۔ جواب: فرق واضح ہے کہ معنی اصولیین خطاب اللہ ہے اور خطاب اللہ من صفات اللہ ہے تو دریں صورت حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ ہو کر صفتہ اللہ ہوگا اور حکم بمعنی ما ثبت بالخطاب یہ فعل مکلف کی صفت ہے تو خلاصہ فرق یہ ہے کہ حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ صفہ اللہ ہے اور حکم بمعنی ما ثبت حالانکہ مصدر کا معنی بھی مصدری ہونا چاہئے ۔ جواب ! مصنف خود جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ حقیقہ تو حکم مصدر ہے لیکن یہاں مصدر کو منی لمفعول (اسم مفعول) کے معنی میں نقل کیا گیا مجازا تو حکم بمعنی ما حکم به وما خوطب یہ یا محکوم بہ کے ہوگا جیسے خلق کو مجاز امخلوق کے معنی میں کیا گیا۔ اب یہ معنی مجازی ( ما ثبت بالخطاب ) فقہاء کے ہاں شائع ذائع مشہور و معروف ہو چکا ہے لہذا اس کو منقول اصطلاحی کہا جائے گا اور منقول اصطلاحی حقیقت اصطلاحی ہوتی ہے اب حکم بمعنی خطاب الله با عتبار لغت حقیقت لیکن باعتبار اصطلاح مجاز ہے اور حکم بمعنی ما خوطب به ) باعتبار اصطلاح حقیقت باعتبار لغت مجاز ہے۔
For example, the declining of the sun is a cause for prayer. Outwardly, it states causality, but implicitly it includes an implication of action. Its meaning would be: when the declining of the sun occurs, prayer becomes obligatory. The obligation of action is from the category of implication. Thus, the wad'i ruling entered into implication, and the definition of hukm became comprehensive by including both its types. Therefore, there is no need for the qayd of 'al-wad'i'. But 'the truth is the first' – the author is stating his opinion, that in my view the correct position is that the definition of hukm must include the qayd of 'al-wad'i' so that the definition encompasses both types. As for the argument of the other group that the wad'i ruling is included in implication, the author responds that including wad'i ruling in implication is not correct because the two, in terms of meaning and reality, are mutually interpretive and distinct. Because the meaning of taklifi is 'the address of Allah related to...' and the meaning of wad'i is 'the relation of something to another thing'. Therefore, including one into the other is not correct; rather, it is necessary to mention each independently. However, in some cases, these two are necessary concomitants of each other; one ruling necessitates the other. For example, the causality of the declining of the sun entails the obligation of prayer, but this does not necessitate that they become identical – union is one thing and entailment is another. Therefore, the author declared the first opinion as preponderant. And some (later Ash'aris) defined shar'i hukm as such (i.e., by khitab Allah). Previously, the author stated that some Ash'aris define absolute hukm (simple hukm) without the qayd of 'shar'i' as 'khitab Allah ta'ala...'. Now he is stating that some later Ash'aris do not define absolute hukm in this way, but rather define shar'i hukm (a hukm that is also shar'i) – i.e., hukm restricted by the qayd of 'al-shar'i' – with 'khitab Allah...'. Therefore, in this case, the definition of absolute hukm will not be 'khitab Allah ta'ala', but rather the definition of absolute hukm would be 'the ascription of one thing to another'. And the jurists use it for what is established by the address (ma thabata bil-khitab). The previous definition was according to the usuliyyun; now the author is presenting the definition of the fuqaha. According to the fuqaha, the definition of hukm is 'what is established by the address' – a thing established by the address, e.g., 'Establish prayer' – from this, the obligation of prayer is established; so the obligation is called hukm. Question: What is the difference between the meaning of the fuqaha and the meaning of the usuliyyun? Answer: The difference is clear: the meaning of the usuliyyun is 'the address of Allah', and the address of Allah is among the attributes of Allah. In that case, hukm in the sense of 'the address of Allah' becomes an attribute of Allah, and hukm in the sense of 'what is established by the address' is an attribute of the act of the obligated person. So the summary of the difference is: hukm in the sense of 'the address of Allah' is an attribute of Allah, and hukm in the sense of 'what is established by the address' is an attribute of the act of Allah's creation. By way of applying the masdar (verbal noun). Answer to an implied question. Question: Hukm is a masdar, so its meaning as 'what is established by the address' is not correct because 'what is established by the address' is not the masdar meaning, but rather the product of the masdar, while the masdar should have a masdar meaning. Answer: The author himself responds: The reality is that hukm is a masdar, but here the masdar has been transferred metaphorically to the meaning of the passive participle (ism maf'ul), so hukm means 'that which is judged' or 'that which is addressed', like 'khalq' (creation) is used metaphorically for 'makhluq' (created thing). Now this metaphorical meaning (what is established by the address) has become widespread and well-known among the fuqaha, so it is called a transmitted technical term, and a transmitted technical term is a technical reality. Thus, hukm in the sense of 'the address of Allah' is a reality linguistically but metaphorically in technical usage, and hukm in the sense of 'what one is addressed with' is a reality technically but metaphorically linguistically.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the definition of the term 'hukm' (legal ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author, commenting on the earlier text, first addresses an objection that the definition of hukm does not need the qualifier 'wad'i' (positional) because the wad'i ruling is already included within the category of 'iqtida' (implication) of a taklifi ruling. The counter-example given is the declining of the sun (zawal) being a sabab (cause) for the obligation of prayer: the causation (sababiyya) is wad'i, but it implicitly necessitates (iqtida) the obligation, so the definition of hukm that covers both taklifi and wad'i would be comprehensive without explicitly adding 'wad'i'. However, the author (Sayyid Sharif Jurjani? Actually the author of the commentary is Mulla Jalal?) rejects this, stating that the correct position (al-haqq huwa al-awwal) is that the qualifier 'wad'i' must be explicitly mentioned in the definition because taklifi and wad'i are fundamentally distinct in meaning and reality. The taklifi hukm is a direct address of Allah regarding actions, while the wad'i hukm is a relationship between something and another thing (e.g., causality). They may be mutually entailing in some cases, but they are not identical; union is different from implication. Therefore, both must be mentioned separately. This reflects the Hanafi insistence on precise definition. The passage then discusses the different definitions of hukm among scholars. Some earlier Ash'aris defined absolute hukm (hukm mutlaq) without the 'shar'i' restriction as 'khitab Allah', while later Ash'aris restricted the definition to 'shar'i hukm' (hukm that is specifically legal). The author notes that according to the latter view, absolute hukm would be defined differently (as isnaad amr ila amr akhar). Then he contrasts the usuli definition (hukm as khitab Allah) with the fuqaha definition (hukm as ma thabata bil-khitab, what is established by the address). This leads to a clarification: for usuliyyun, hukm is the divine address itself, an attribute of Allah; for fuqaha, hukm is the resulting obligation or prohibition, an attribute of the mukallaf's act. A question arises: if hukm is a masdar (verbal noun), how can it mean 'what is established' (ma thabata)? The author explains that this is a metaphorical transfer (naql majazi) common in technical terminology: the masdar is used for the object, just as 'khalq' is used for 'makhluq'. This transferred meaning became widespread among jurists, so it is a 'manqul istilahi' (transferred technical term) which is considered a 'haqiqa istilahiyya' (technical reality). So when used by fuqaha, hukm in the sense of 'ma thabata bil-khitab' is technically real, though linguistically metaphorical. Conversely, hukm as 'khitab Allah' is linguistically real but technically metaphorical. This analysis shows the Hanafi concern for precise terminology and the authority of customary usage in defining technical terms.

Key Terms
حكم تكليفي (hukm taklifi): A directive from Allah regarding the actions of the mukallaf that involves a demand (obligation, prohibition, permissibility) or a choice.
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): A ruling that establishes a relationship between something and another, such as causality (sabab), condition (shart), or preventer (mani'), without directly demanding an action.
خطاب الله (khitab Allah): The divine address (Qur'an or Sunnah) that is the source of legal rulings.
ما ثبت بالخطاب (ma thabata bil-khitab): That which is established through the divine address, i.e., the resulting legal value (obligation, prohibition, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in the text, why must the definition of hukm include the qualifier 'al-wad'i'?
A) Because without it, the definition only covers taklifi rulings and excludes wad'i rulings.
B) Because all Ash'aris define hukm without the qualifier.
C) Because wad'i rulings are a subset of taklifi rulings.
D) Because the declining of the sun is a sabab for prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm must explicitly include both taklifi (demand) and wad'i (relational) categories because they are distinct in meaning, and omitting the qualifier conflates entailment with identity.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Dispute on the Definition of Hukm: Ash'ari vs Hanafi View
Taftazani's objection to the author's classification and the response defending the Hanafi position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Ash'ari views on the definition of hukm and evaluate Taftazani's objection using evidence from Shafi'i sources.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm is contested: some Ash'aris define absolute hukm as khitab Allah, others define shar'i hukm.

Definitions are foundational in usul al-fiqh. The term 'hukm' appears in the definition of fiqh itself, yet scholars differed on what exactly is being defined. This dispute between a Hanafi commentator and the famous Ash'ari scholar Taftazani reveals that even within the Ash'ari school, there is nuance: some define absolute hukm (the term used in the definition of fiqh) as the divine address, while others define shar'i hukm (the conventional usuli term) as such. The passage sharpens your understanding of how school positions are not always monolithic and how a single quote from Sharh al-Minhaj can settle the point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions attributed to Ash'aris
The author claims some Ash'aris define 'absolute hukm' (mentioned in the definition of fiqh) as khitab Allah, while other later Ash'aris define 'shar'i hukm' (the conventional usuli term) as khitab Allah.
This is the key distinction contested by Taftazani.
2
Understand Taftazani's objection
Taftazani objects, asserting that all Ash'ari and Shafi'i sources agree that khitab Allah is the definition of shar'i hukm only, not absolute hukm. He accuses the author of having not studied Shafi'i books.
Taftazani's claim rests on an alleged consensus.
3
Locate the Hanafi response's evidence
The Hanafi commentator rebuts by quoting Sharh al-Minhaj: 'the defined term is the shar'i hukm that is fiqh, not absolute shar'i hukm.' This shows that some Ash'aris indeed define the hukm of fiqh (i.e., absolute hukm) as khitab Allah.
Sharh al-Minhaj is a Shafi'i source, undermining Taftazani's claim of unanimity.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if absolute hukm is defined as khitab Allah, then fiqh is knowledge of the divine address itself; if shar'i hukm is defined as khitab Allah, then fiqh is knowledge of the legal rulings derived from the address. The Hanafi view aligns with the latter but acknowledges variation among Ash'aris.
This distinction affects how one understands the subject matter of fiqh.

شرح تلویح قوله ولما عرف الفقه اقول المذكور فى كتب الشافعية غرض شارح تفتازانی اعتراض على المصنف ہے ! حاصل اشکال یہ ہے کہ آپ نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ خطاب اللہ تعالی کو مطلق حکم کی تعریف قرار دتے ہیں جو مطلق حکم ماخوذ و مذکور فی تعریف الفقہ ہے اور بعض اشاعرہ خطاب اللہ کو حکم شرعی جو متعارف بین الاصولیین ہے اس کی تعریف قرار دیتے ہیں یہ جو آپ نے معرف میں اشاعرہ کے اختلاف کو ذکر کیا ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ کے نزدیک معرف مطلق حکم ہے بعض کے نزدیک معرف حکم شرعی ہے یہ بالکل غلط ہے بلکہ تمام کتب شافعیہ واشاعرہ کا اتفاق ہے کہ خطاب اللہ تعالی التعلق با فعال مکلفین اس حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے جو متعارف بین الاصولیین ہے نہ کہ اس حکم ( مطلق) کی جو تعریف فقہ میں ماخوذ و مذکور ہے لہذا مصنف کا قیل وقیل کہنا غلط ہے مصنف سے یہ غلطی ہوئی کہ انہوں نے یہ کہدیا کہ خطاب اللہ اس حکم مطلق کی تعریف ہے جو فقہ میں مذکور ہے اور شرعی کی قید زائد ہے معرف میں اس کا کوئی دخل نہیں ہے اور یہ بھی کہدیا کہ خطاب اللہ کا حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہونا اشاعرہ کی رائے ہے حالانکہ یہ تینوں باتیں غلط ہیں چونکہ مصنف نے کتب شوافع کا مطالعہ نہیں کیا اس لیے اس سے یہ غلطی ہو گئی ۔ جواب ! شارح تفتازانی کو اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ اولا تو آپ کا یہ قول المذکور فی کتب الشافعیہ غلط ہے کیونکہ کتب شافعیہ میں کہیں بھی اس طرح مذکور نہیں ہے جس طرح آپ نے کہا ہے اگر المذ کور کی بجائے المفہوم کہتا تو لکان اولی نیز مصنف کی بات بالکل درست ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ کے نزدیک اس حکم مطلق کی تعریف ہے جو مذکور فی تعریف الفقہ ہے چنانچہ شرح منہاج کی عبارت ملاحظہ فرمائیں۔ واجاب بعضهم بان المحدود الحكم الشرعي الذي هو فقه لا مطلق الحكم الشرعی یہ عبارت صاف دلالت کر رہی ہے کہ خطاب اللہ حکم فقہی کہ تعریف ہے نہ حکم شرعی کی فنقول عرف بعض الاشاعرة الحكم الشرعي بهذا اى بخطاب الله المتعلق بافعال المكلفين یہاں سے شارح حکم بمعنی خطاب اللہ کے الفاظ کی تشریح کرنا چاہتے ہیں سب سے پہلے یہ وضاحت کر دی کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے حکم شرعی کی تعریف خطاب اللہ کے ساتھ کی ہے ( اعتراض شارح تفتازانی صاحب نے ابھی ابھی گذشتہ
Sharh al-Talwih: His statement: 'And when fiqh was defined...' I say: What is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is – the intention of the commentator Taftazani is an objection against the author. The summary of the objection is that you stated that some Ash'aris make 'khitab Allah ta'ala' the definition of absolute hukm, which is taken and mentioned in the definition of fiqh, and some Ash'aris make it the definition of shar'i hukm, which is conventional among the usuliyyun. This statement of yours – that there is a difference of opinion among the Ash'aris regarding what is defined – is completely false. Rather, all the books of the Shafi'is and Ash'aris agree that 'khitab Allah ta'ala al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin' is the definition of shar'i hukm, which is conventional among the usuliyyun, not the definition of that absolute hukm which is taken and mentioned in the definition of fiqh. Therefore, the author's statement of 'some say and some say' is wrong. The author made a mistake when he said that 'khitab Allah' is the definition of absolute hukm mentioned in fiqh, and that the qayd of 'shar'i' is extra and has no role in the definition, and also said that making 'khitab Allah' the definition of shar'i hukm is an opinion of the Ash'aris, whereas these three things are false. Since the author did not study the books of the Shafi'is, this error occurred. Response: The commentator Taftazani is answered as follows: Firstly, your statement 'what is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is' is false, because nowhere in Shafi'i books is it mentioned as you said. If he had said 'what is understood' instead of 'what is mentioned', it would have been better. Moreover, the author's statement is absolutely correct: according to some Ash'aris, it is the definition of that absolute hukm which is mentioned in the definition of fiqh. As such, consider the passage from Sharh al-Minhaj: 'And some responded that what is defined is the shar'i hukm that is fiqh, not absolute shar'i hukm.' This passage clearly indicates that 'khitab Allah' is the definition of the fiqh hukm, not of shar'i hukm. So we say: Some Ash'aris defined shar'i hukm as such, i.e., by 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin'. From here, the commentator intends to explain the words of 'hukm' meaning 'khitab Allah'. First, he clarifies that some Ash'aris defined shar'i hukm with 'khitab Allah'. (The objection of the commentator Taftazani has just been mentioned previously...)

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the author (the Hanafi commentator) and the commentator Taftazani (a famous Ash'ari/Shafi'i scholar). The author had earlier stated that some Ash'aris define 'absolute hukm' (the hukm mentioned in the definition of fiqh) as 'khitab Allah', while other later Ash'aris define 'shar'i hukm' (the hukm conventional among usuliyyun) as such. Taftazani objects, claiming that all Ash'ari and Shafi'i sources agree that 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin' is the definition of shar'i hukm, not absolute hukm. He accuses the author of misrepresenting the Ash'ari position and of not having studied Shafi'i books. The Hanafi response defends the author: first, Taftazani's claim about what is 'mentioned' in Shafi'i books is itself incorrect; second, the author's statement is supported by evidence from Sharh al-Minhaj, which explicitly says that the defined term is 'shar'i hukm that is fiqh' (i.e., the hukm studied in fiqh), not absolute shar'i hukm. Thus, there is a nuance: some Ash'aris define the hukm that is the subject of fiqh (which is a specific type of shar'i hukm) as khitab Allah. The passage illustrates a typical usuli debate where scholars from different schools contest the precise definitional scope. The Hanafi commentator insists on the accuracy of dividing Ash'ari opinions, showing careful attention to textual evidence.

Key Terms
حكم مطلق (hukm mutlaq): The absolute, unrestricted term 'hukm' as used in the definition of fiqh (knowledge of the hukm).
حكم شرعي (hukm shar'i): The legal ruling that is the subject of usul al-fiqh, conventionally defined as 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the response to Taftazani's objection, what evidence supports the author's claim that some Ash'aris define absolute hukm as khitab Allah?
A) A passage from Sharh al-Minhaj stating that the defined term is the shar'i hukm that is fiqh, not absolute shar'i hukm.
B) The consensus of all Shafi'i books.
C) Taftazani's own admission.
D) The definition of fiqh itself.

Key Takeaway
Taftazani's claim of consensus among Ash'aris is rebutted by quoting Sharh al-Minhaj, showing that there are two Ash'ari views on the definition of hukm.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition of Hukm: The Dispute with Taftazani
Critical refinement of the definition of hukm and response to Taftazani's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two definitions of hukm (absolute vs legal) and evaluate the Ash'ari disagreement regarding the defined term of khitab Allah.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm as khitab Allah is not unanimous among Ash'aris; some define absolute ruling, others legal ruling.

This passage from Misk al-Malih delves into a key usul al-fiqh debate: whether the term 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh refers to absolute ruling (hukm mutlaq) or legal ruling (hukm shar'i). The commentator defends the author's position against al-Taftazani's objection, revealing that Ash'ari scholars themselves differ. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how definitions shape fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of hukm
Recognize that the author states some Ash'aris define khitab Allah as hukm mutlaq (used in fiqh definition) and others as hukm shar'i (common among usul scholars).
Note the distinction between the term used in fiqh vs. usul.
2
Understand Taftazani's objection
Taftazani claims all Ash'ari/Shafi'i sources agree that khitab Allah defines only hukm shar'i, rejecting any difference.
This is the critique the author must refute.
3
Analyze the four Hanafi responses
Study each response: (1) Taftazani misreads Shafi'i books; (2) Some Ash'aris implicitly accept the definition; (3) Those using 'absolute' mean legal; (4) Disagreement is in the wording of the definition, not the defined term.
Each response shows a different angle of defense.
4
Trace the linguistic analysis of khitab
Follow how the commentator explains 'khitab' as transferred from verbal noun to speech (kalam), and the debate on whether eternal speech qualifies as khitab.
This clarifies the nature of Divine address.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If hukm is defined as mutlaq, fiqh is knowledge of absolute khitab; if as shar'i, fiqh is knowledge of legal ruling only.
Affects the scope of fiqh as a discipline.

And the commentary al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Misk al-Malih. It [the term] and what is addressed (ma khutiba bihi) or the object of the ruling (mahkum bihi) becomes like 'khalq' used metaphorically in the sense of 'makhluq'. Now this metaphorical meaning (ma thabata bil-khitab) has become widespread and well-known among jurists, so it is called a transmitted conventional term (manqul istilahi), and a transmitted conventional term is a conventional reality (haqiqah istilahiyyah). Now, 'hukm' in the sense of khitab Allah is a reality linguistically but a metaphor conventionally, and 'hukm' in the sense of 'what is addressed by it' (ma khutiba bihi) is a reality conventionally and a metaphor linguistically. Commentary on al-Talwih: His statement: 'When fiqh is defined...' I say that what is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is is an objection by the commentator al-Taftazani against the author. The gist of the objection is: You have stated that some Ash'aris take the address of Allah (khitab Allah) as the definition of absolute ruling (hukm mutlaq) which is taken and mentioned in the definition of fiqh, and some Ash'aris take khitab Allah as the definition of legal ruling (hukm shar'i) which is common among usul scholars. This mention of difference among the Ash'aris regarding the defined term is completely wrong. Rather, all the books of the Shafi'is and Ash'aris agree that khitab Allah connected to the actions of the legally responsible persons is the definition of legal ruling (hukm shar'i) which is common among usul scholars, not the definition of that absolute ruling (hukm mutlaq) which is taken and mentioned in the definition of fiqh. Therefore, the author's saying 'some say, some say' is wrong. The author made a mistake by stating that khitab Allah is the definition of the absolute ruling mentioned in fiqh, and that the qualification 'shar'i' is superfluous with no role in the definition, and also that the definition of legal ruling by khitab Allah is the view of the Ash'aris – all three statements are wrong. Since the author did not study the books of the Shafi'is, he made this mistake. Reply: The commentator al-Taftazani has been given a response to this objection: firstly, your statement 'what is mentioned in the books of the Shafi'is' is wrong, because in the Shafi'i books it is not mentioned in the way you said. If you had said 'what is understood' instead of 'what is mentioned', it would have been better. Also, the author’s statement is completely correct: some Ash'aris take this as the definition of the absolute ruling that is mentioned in the definition of fiqh. Consider the text of Sharh al-Minhaj: 'And some answered that the limited object is the legal ruling which is fiqh, not the absolute legal ruling.' This text clearly indicates that khitab Allah is the definition of the fiqh ruling, not the legal ruling. So we say: Some Ash'aris defined legal ruling by this, i.e., by khitab Allah connected to actions of the legally responsible persons. Here the commentator wants to explain the words 'hukm in the sense of khitab Allah'. First, he clarifies that some Ash'aris defined legal ruling by khitab Allah. (Objection: The commentator al-Taftazani just now in the previous passage strongly refuted the author, stating that khitab Allah is in the view of all Ash'aris the definition of legal ruling, and attributing it to only some Ash'aris is incorrect. But here he himself said: 'Some Ash'aris defined legal ruling by khitab Allah.' So he fell into what he had objected to the author. The commentator should not have mentioned the word 'some'; he should have said: 'Thus the Ash'aris defined...' Reply: Some people have given this response to the objection raised against Taftazani: 'fa-naqul' is not the first person plural; rather the expression is 'fa-yaqul', and the pronoun in 'yaqul' refers to the author. But this response is flawed because in all copies the expression is 'fa-naqul' (with nun). Also, the author did not mention this definition because the definition that Taftazani transmitted goes up to 'al-mukallafin', while the author's definition later ends at 'aw al-takhyir'. Reply (2): Taftazani's expression intends that some Ash'aris mentioned this definition, and some did not mention it but agreed with it and accepted it. Reply (3): The intent is that some Ash'aris defined this as legal ruling, and some as absolute ruling, but they meant by absolute ruling also the legal ruling. Reply (4): The commentator Taftazani's intent is that all Ash'aris agree that khitab Allah is the defined term of legal ruling, but there is disagreement in the definition: some define legal ruling up to 'al-mukallafin', some up to 'aw al-takhyir', and some add the restriction of 'aw al-wad'i'. So the restriction of 'some Ash'aris' is with regard to the definition, not with regard to the defined term, because the defined term is by consensus legal ruling. But this response is far from the apparent meaning of the commentator's expression. And Allah knows best what is correct. 'And khitab in language...' From here the commentator al-Taftazani wants to explain the linguistic and metaphorical intended meanings of 'khitab'. Thus he says: The linguistic meaning of 'khitab' is 'directing speech toward another for comprehension' (tawjeeh al-kalam nahwa al-ghayr li al-ifham). So in its linguistic sense, 'khitab' is a verbal noun (masdar) with a masdar meaning, but the masdar meaning cannot be intended here. Therefore, the masdar is transferred to mean 'that by which addressing occurs' (ma yaqa'u bihi al-takhatub) or 'what is addressed by it' (ma khutiba bihi) or the locus of addressing which is called speech (kalam). So now 'khitab' means speech, and here it means intended meaning: here it is 'that by which addressing occurs' and speech, intending the eternal speech (kalam nafsi) which is the attribute of Allah. 'And whoever holds that speech is not called...' The purpose of the commentator is to answer an anticipated question. The question is: You have taken 'khitab' to mean 'that by which addressing occurs' and then you said that it means eternal speech – this is incorrect, because the term 'khitab' does not apply to eternal speech, as in pre-eternity there was no addressee to be addressed. Response: 'And whoever holds' answers this problem: there are two schools: one school holds that the word 'khitab' applies to eternal speech, it is also called khitab, and the definition of khitab also applies to it. (2) Some people say that the definition of khitab is 'directing speech' (tawjeeh al-kalam).
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, focusing on the definition of 'hukm' (ruling) in usul al-fiqh. The author distinguishes between the absolute ruling (hukm mutlaq) used in the definition of fiqh and the legal ruling (hukm shar'i) common among usul scholars. He states that some Ash'aris define hukm mutlaq as khitab Allah (the address of Allah), while others define hukm shar'i as such. The commentator al-Taftazani objects, asserting that all Ash'aris agree on khitab Allah as the definition of hukm shar'i. The passage then provides four responses defending the author's position: (1) Taftazani's claim about Shafi'i books is inaccurate; the author's view appears in Sharh al-Minhaj. (2) Some Ash'aris explicitly state this definition, others implicitly accept it. (3) Those who define hukm mutlaq actually mean hukm shar'i. (4) The disagreement is over the wording of the definition, not the defined term. The passage then delves into the linguistic analysis of 'khitab', explaining that in this context it means the eternal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah, and addresses the objection that eternal speech cannot be 'addressing' since there was no addressee in pre-eternity. It mentions two positions: one affirming that 'khitab' applies to eternal speech, and one reserving it for temporal addressing.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In this context, hukm is defined as khitab Allah (the address of Allah) related to the actions of the legally responsible persons.
خطاب (khitab): Linguistically means directing speech to another for understanding; terminologically it means the speech itself (kalam) and is used for the eternal attribute of speech.
حقيقة (haqiqah): Reality: a word used for its original meaning. Here, 'hukm' as khitab Allah is haqiqah linguistically, but majaz (metaphor) conventionally.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage; e.g., 'khalq' used for 'makhluq'. The text discusses metaphorical transfer of meaning.
منقول اصطلاحي (manqul istilahi): A term that has been transferred from its linguistic meaning to a conventional meaning among a group; it becomes a conventional reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, how do some Ash'aris define 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh?
A) As khitab Allah related to actions of the mukallafin (legal ruling).
B) As khitab Allah without further qualification (absolute ruling).
C) As the eternal speech of Allah (kalam nafsi).
D) As the object of the ruling (mahkum bihi).

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm as khitab Allah is contested among Ash'ari scholars; some define it as absolute ruling (for fiqh) and others as legal ruling (for usul), and understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying usul al-fiqh definitions.

The Definition of Hukm Shar'i as Khitab Allah: Addressing Objections
Commentary analyzing the Ash'ari definition of Hukm Shar'i and resolving objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Ash'ari definition of hukm shar'i, explain how 'khitab' is interpreted as kalam nafsi, and apply the Hanafi principle of jam' al-jins to resolve the comprehensiveness objection.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's address relating to action; the address is internal speech, and 'actions of the mukallafin' is a generic plural applying to any single act.

This lesson unpacks a dense commentary from Misk al-Malih on the definition of hukm shar'i. We will navigate through an internal Ash'ari dispute about the definition's attribution, delve into the linguistic and theological meaning of 'khitab', and tackle two key objections: how eternal speech can be an 'address', and how the plural 'actions of the legally responsible' can include rulings for individuals. By the end, you will not only understand the definition but also see how Hanafi usul principles like jam' al-jins safeguard its comprehensiveness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and the attribution dispute
Locate the Ash'ari definition of hukm shar'i as 'khitab Allah'. Note the author's criticism of attributing it only to 'some' Ash'aris and the responses defending Taftazani's wording.
The final response distinguishes between the defined concept (agreed) and the wording of the definition (varied).
2
Analyze the shift in meaning of 'khitab'
Trace how 'khitab' moves from its literal meaning (verbal noun: addressing) to a transferred meaning (that by which address occurs, i.e., speech/kalam). Determine why this shift is necessary for the definition.
The literal meaning cannot apply to an eternal attribute; thus a metaphorical transfer (majaz) is used.
3
Examine the objection about eternity and the two schools
Understand the objection: how can kalam nafsi be called 'khitab' when no addressee existed? Review the two schools: one applying 'khitab' directly, the other modifying the definition to include intention (qasd al-ifham).
The commentator adopts the latter: intention to make understand suffices; addressee existence at time of intention is unnecessary.
4
Apply the jam' al-jins principle to the plural objection
Recognize that 'af'al al-mukallafin' uses two plural forms. Apply the Hanafi rule that a definite plural (with al- or idafah to a definite plural) becomes a generic plural, thus applying to a single action of a single mukallaf.
This preserves comprehensiveness, including rulings specific to the Prophet.
5
Confirm the definition's comprehensiveness
Test the definition with examples: general rulings like 'prayer is obligatory' and specific rulings like the Prophet's permission for more than four wives. See that both are covered.
The definition remains sound and includes all individuals of hukm.

افعال جمع سے جنس فعل مراد ہوگی اور الملفین سے جنس مکلف مراد ہو گا اب التعلق با فعال المکلفین کا معنی ہوگا حکم وہ خطاب اللہ ہے جو جنس مکلف کے کسی ایک فعل کے ساتھ متعلق ہو اب تعریف صحیح ہوگی اور دونوں خرابیاں دفع ہو جائیں گی تعریف جامع جمیع
In the expression, the author strongly denies that the address of Allah Almighty is the definition of legal ruling according to all Ash'aris; attributing it only to some Ash'aris is incorrect. But here he himself said: 'Some Ash'aris defined legal ruling as the address of Allah.' So he fell into what he criticized on the author. The commentator Taftazani should not have mentioned the word 'some'; he should have said: 'So the Ash'aris defined...' Response: Some scholars answered the objection against Taftazani by saying that 'fa-naqul' is not a first-person plural form, but the expression is 'fa-yaqul', and the pronoun in 'yaqul' refers to the author. But this answer is weak because in all copies the expression is 'fa-naqul' (with nun), and also the author did not mention this definition because the definition Taftazani transmitted goes up to 'al-mukallafin', while the author's definition later ends with 'aw al-takhyir'. Response (2): The purpose of Taftazani's expression is that some Ash'aris mentioned this definition, and some did not mention it but agreed with it and accepted it. Response (3): The intent is that some Ash'aris defined this as legal ruling, and some defined absolute ruling, but by absolute ruling they also meant legal ruling. Response (4): The commentator Taftazani's purpose is that all Ash'aris agree that the address of Allah is the definition of legal ruling; however, there is disagreement in the definition. Some Ash'aris define legal ruling up to 'al-mukallafin', some up to 'aw al-takhyir', and some add the condition 'aw al-wad'. So the restriction 'some Ash'aris' is with respect to the definition, not the defined, because the defined by consensus is legal ruling. But this answer is far from the apparent meaning of the commentator's expression, and Allah knows best. And 'khitab' in language... From here, the commentator Taftazani intends to explain the linguistic, metaphorical, or intended meaning of 'khitab'. Thus he said: The linguistic meaning of 'khitab' is directing speech towards another for understanding. So according to the linguistic meaning, 'khitab' is a verbal noun; its meaning is verbal-noun meaning, but the verbal-noun meaning cannot be intended here. Therefore, here the verbal noun is transferred to 'ma yaqa'u bihi al-takhatub' (that by which mutual address occurs) or 'ma khutiba bihi' (that with which one is addressed) or the place of address, which is called speech. Thus now 'khitab' means speech, and 'wa huwa huna' he explains the intended meaning: that here 'ma yaqa'u bihi al-takhatub' and speech refer to internal speech, which is an attribute of Allah. 'And whoever holds that speech is not called...' The commentator's purpose is to answer an anticipated question. Question: You took 'khitab' to mean 'ma yaqa'u bihi al-takhatub', and then you said that it means internal eternal speech. This is wrong, because internal eternal speech cannot be described as 'khitab', since in eternity there was no addressee to be addressed. Answer: With 'wa man dhahaba' he answers this objection, that in reality there are two schools: one school holds that the word 'khitab' applies to eternal speech; it is called 'khitab' and the definition of 'khitab' applies to it. (2) Some say that the definition of 'khitab' (directing speech) does not apply to internal eternal speech, but only to verbal speech. Therefore, they slightly modified the definition of 'khitab'. They gave two definitions: (1) Speech directed for understanding, (2) Speech intended from it to make understand one who is ready to understand. Now these two definitions apply to both verbal speech and internal speech, because the intention of making understand is related to internal speech; verbal speech is merely a means and instrument to make internal speech understood. Objection: These definitions also do not apply to internal eternal speech, because the first definition was 'speech directed for understanding', and 'making understand' occurs only when there is an addressee present who understands, whereas in eternity there was no addressee. Similarly, the second definition also does not apply to internal eternal speech, because 'the intended from it to make understand one who is ready to understand' requires that at the time of address an addressee ready for understanding exists, whereas in eternity there was no addressee. Answer: Both definitions apply to internal eternal speech, because intending to make understand one who is ready for understanding does not require that he be present at the time of intention; rather, when the making understand actually occurs, at that time the existence and presence of that ready one is necessary. At the time of intending to make understand, neither existence nor presence is necessary. In summary, for calling internal speech 'khitab' in eternity, the existence of an addressee is not necessary. 'And the meaning of its connection with the actions of the legally responsible...' The commentator's purpose is to answer an anticipated question. Question: The definition of 'hukm' is not comprehensive; it does not apply to any of its individuals because 'al-ta'alluq bi af'al al-mukallafin' uses 'af'al' plural and 'mukallafin' plural. So the intent would be that 'hukm' is the address of Allah that connects with all actions of all legally responsible persons. But there is no such address of Allah that is related to all actions of all legally responsible persons. Thus two problems arise: first, the definition is not comprehensive, not applying to any individual of 'hukm'; second, this problem arises: special privileges of the Prophet would be excluded from the definition, e.g., 'ibahat al-nikah ma fawq al-arba'ah' is specific to the Prophet, so this address is not related to all legally responsible persons but only to a single legally responsible person (the Prophet). Answer: The gist of the answer is that here 'af'al' is plural and it is added to 'al-mukallafin', and that is also plural definite with lam. The rule is that when a plural is definite with lam, or is added to a plural definite with lam, its plurality is nullified and it becomes like a generic plural, applicable to a single individual. Therefore, here 'af'al' plural means the genus of action, and 'al-mukallafin' means the genus of legally responsible person. Now 'al-ta'alluq bi af'al al-mukallafin' means 'hukm' is the address of Allah that is connected to a single action of the genus of legally responsible person. Now the definition is correct, and both problems are removed; the definition encompasses all.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from Misk al-Malih on the definition of hukm shar'i (legal ruling) as 'khitab Allah' (the address of Allah), which is a definition attributed to some Ash'aris. The commentator, Taftazani, is criticized by the author of the matn for attributing the definition only to some Ash'aris when all Ash'aris actually accept it. Four responses are given to defend Taftazani, with the final one being the most plausible: the restriction 'some' refers to differences in the precise wording of the definition, not the defined concept itself. The commentator then delves into the linguistic and technical meaning of 'khitab', explaining that in this context it does not mean the verbal noun 'addressing' but rather 'that by which address occurs', i.e., speech (kalam). This speech is further identified as kalam nafsi (internal speech), an eternal attribute of Allah. A major objection arises: how can kalam nafsi be called 'khitab' in eternity when there was no addressee? Two schools are presented: one holds that 'khitab' applies to kalam nafsi directly; the other modifies the definition of 'khitab' to include kalam nafsi by focusing on the intention of making understand (qasd al-ifham) rather than the actual presence of an addressee. The answer affirms that kalam nafsi can be called 'khitab' because the intention to make understand does not require the addressee's existence at the time of intention. The passage then addresses the objection that the definition 'ta'alluq bi af'al al-mukallafin' (connection with the actions of the legally responsible) is not comprehensive because 'af'al' and 'mukallafin' are plural. The response uses the Hanafi usul principle that a plural noun made definite by al- or by idafah to a definite plural loses its plurality and becomes a generic plural (jam' al-jins), thus applying to a single action of a single mukallaf. This preserves the comprehensiveness of the definition, including rulings specific to the Prophet.

Key Terms
خطاب (khitab): In the definition of hukm, it means 'address' or 'speech' (kalam), specifically kalam nafsi (internal speech) as an attribute of Allah.
کلام نفسی (kalam nafsi): Internal speech, an eternal attribute of Allah, distinguished from kalam lafzi (verbal speech) which is created.
تعلق (ta'alluq): Connection or relation; in the definition of hukm, it means the address of Allah is related to the actions of the mukallaf.
جمع جنس (jam' al-jins): A generic plural that indicates the genus and can apply to a single instance; used to resolve the objection about plurality in the definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the commentator resolve the problem that the plural 'af'al al-mukallafin' makes the definition not apply to rulings for a single mukallaf?
A) He argues the definition only applies to general rulings.
B) He invokes the principle of jam' al-jins (generic plural).
C) He adds a condition that the address must be to all mukallafin.
D) He rejects the definition as incorrect.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah' is comprehensive when 'khitab' is interpreted as internal speech and 'af'al al-mukallafin' as a generic plural.
