Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Defining Khatab and Its Application to Internal Speech
Definition of khatab with defense of its applicability to kalam nafsi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of khatab and explain why it applies to kalam nafsi in pre-eternity.

Core Idea
Khatab is defined by intention to make understood, not by the presence of an addressee.

In Hanafi usul, the definition of 'khatab' (address) is crucial for understanding how Allah's eternal attribute of speech (kalam nafsi) constitutes a command or address. Some scholars initially defined khatab narrowly as verbal speech directed to a present listener, which would exclude pre-eternal speech. This lesson examines the refined definitions that extend khatab to internal speech, and the key argument that intention (qasd) suffices for the term to apply, even when no addressee exists at the moment of intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions of khatab
Read the two definitions given in the passage. The first is 'speech directed for understanding' (al-kalam al-muwajjah li al-afham). The second is 'speech intended to make understood one who is prepared to understand' (al-kalam al-maqsud minh ifham man huwa mutahayyi' li fahmih).
Both definitions shift the focus from mere utterance to the intention behind the speech.
2
Understand the objection against applying these definitions to pre-eternal kalam nafsi
The objection states that in pre-eternity (azal), there was no addressee present. The definitions appear to require an addressee who understands (mutahayyi' li al-fahm). Since no creature existed then, how can Allah's eternal speech be called khatab?
This objection highlights a potential tension between divine attribute and temporal creation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes between the time of intending to make understood and the time of actual making understood. The definition (especially the second) requires only an intention to make understood to someone who is capable, not that the addressee exists at the moment of intention. The presence of the addressee becomes necessary only when the actual communication (ifham bi al-fi'l) occurs.
Thus, Allah's eternal intention to address future beings suffices for calling His eternal speech 'khatab'.
4
Connect to the broader Hanafi position on kalam nafsi
The Hanafi school affirms that Allah's speech is an eternal attribute (kalam nafsi) distinct from created verbal expressions. This definition of khatab supports that view by showing that address does not depend on temporal factors like a listener's presence.
This usul point underpins the doctrine of the Quran being uncreated in its essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسک الملیح کلام نفسی از لی پر صادق نہیں آتی صرف کلام لفظی پر صادق آتی ہے اس لیے ان حضرات نے خطاب کی تعریف میں تھوڑ اسارد و بدل کیا ہے انہوں نے خطاب کی دو تعریفیں کی ہیں (۱) الكلام الموجه للأفهام یعنی وہ کلام جو متوجہ کی جائے سمجھانے کیلئے (۲) هو الكلام المقصود منه افهام من هو متهيء لفهمه يعنی خطاب وہ کلام ہے جس سے مقصود اس شخص کو سمجھانا ہو جو سمجھنے کیلئے تیار ہو اب یہ دو تعریفی کلام لفظی اور کلام نفسی دونوں پر صادق آ رہی ہیں کیونکہ قصد افہام کا تعلق ہوتا ہی کلام نفسی کے ساتھ ہے کلام لفظی تو کلام نفسی کو سمجھانے کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ ہوتی ہے سوال : یہ ہوتا ہے کہ خطاب کی یہ تعریفیں بھی کلام نفسی از لی پر صادق نہیں آتیں کیونکہ اول تعریف تھی الکلام الموجه للا فہام تو افہام اور سمجھانا تب ہو گا جب کوئی مخاطب سمجھنے والا بھی موجود و حاضر ہو حالانکہ ازل میں تو کوئی مخاطب موجود نہیں تھا اسی طرح تعریف ثانی بھی کلام نفسی از لی پر صادق نہیں آتی کیونکہ (المقصود منه افهام من هو متهيء لفهمه ) اس بات کو مقتضی ہے کہ بوقت خطاب کوئی مخاطب متهيء لفهمه موجود ہو حالانکہ ازل میں تو کوئی مخاطب نہیں تھانہ جواب یہ دونوں تعریفیں کلام از لی نفسی پر صادق آرہی ہیں کیونکہ متهنيء لفهمہ کیلئے ارادہ افہام کرتا اس بات کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا کہ وہ بوقت قصد و ارادہ بھی موجود و حاضر ہو بلکہ جب افہام بالفعل ہوگا تو اس وقت اس متھنی للفھم کا وجود و حضور ضروری ہوگا بوقت ارادہ افہام نہ وجود ضروری ہے اور نہ حضور خلاصہ ایس کہ ازل میں کلام نفسی کو خطاب کہنے کیلئے کسی مخاطب کا موجود ہونا کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے
Internal speech [kalam nafsi] does not apply to pre-eternity, only verbal speech applies. So these scholars slightly changed the definition of address. They gave two definitions: (1) Speech directed for understanding, i.e., speech that is directed for comprehension. (2) It is speech intended to make understood one who is prepared to understand. Now these two definitions apply to both verbal and internal speech, because the intention of making understood is related to internal speech; verbal speech is merely a means to convey internal speech. Question: These definitions of address also do not apply to internal speech in pre-eternity, because the first definition is 'speech directed for understanding' - understanding occurs only when an addressee who understands is present, while in pre-eternity there was no addressee. Similarly, the second definition also does not apply to internal speech in pre-eternity because 'intended to make understood one who is prepared to understand' requires that at the time of address an addressee prepared to understand is present, while in pre-eternity there was no addressee. Answer: Both definitions apply to internal speech in pre-eternity, because intending to make understood for one prepared does not require that he be present at the time of intention; rather, when actual making understood occurs, at that time the existence and presence of the one prepared for understanding is necessary. At the time of intending to make understood, neither existence nor presence is necessary. Summary: Thus, in pre-eternity, for internal speech to be called address, it is not necessary for any addressee to exist.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the term 'khatab' (address) in the context of kalam nafsi (internal speech). The author explains that some scholars modified the definition of khatab to include internal speech, which is eternal. They gave two definitions focusing on the intention to make understood. The objection that in pre-eternity there was no addressee is answered: the definition requires only the intention to make understood to one who is capable, not that the addressee exists at the time of the intention. Thus, Allah's eternal speech is properly called khatab. This is a key point in Hanafi kalam to affirm the attribute of speech.

Key Terms
خطاب (khatab): Speech directed for understanding, intended to make understood one who is prepared
کلام نفسی (kalam nafsi): Internal speech, an eternal attribute of Allah
کلام لفظی (kalam lafzi): Verbal speech, the created expression of internal meaning

Defending the Definition of Hukm: The Rule of Jama‘ Mu’arraf bi al-Lam
Defense of definition using grammatical rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a plural defined by 'al' indicates genus to defend the comprehensiveness of a definition.

Core Idea
A plural defined by 'al' indicates genus, not universality—saving the definition of hukm from its own apparent plural.

The definition of hukm as 'the speech of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible persons' seems to contain two plurals: 'actions' and 'legally responsible persons'. A critic might object that no single divine address relates to all actions of all persons, so the definition fails. But the Hanafi scholar reveals a subtle grammatical principle that turns the apparent flaw into strength.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Notice that 'actions' (af‘āl) is plural and annexed to 'legally responsible persons' (al-mukallafīn), also a plural defined by 'al'. A literal reading demands that hukm relate to ALL actions of ALL persons, which is impossible.
The objection claims the definition is not comprehensive (ghayr jāmi‘) and excludes specific rulings for the Prophet.
2
Recognize the two defects
If the plurals are taken universally, (1) the definition applies to no actual divine address, and (2) rulings specific to the Prophet (e.g., permissibility of marrying more than four) would be excluded because they relate only to one person.
These defects would render the definition useless.
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
According to Hanafi usul, a plural noun defined by 'al' (jam‘ mu’arraf bi al-lam) or annexed to such a plural indicates the genus (jins), not universal quantification. Thus, 'actions' means 'any action' and 'legally responsible persons' means 'any such person'.
This rule is a key tool in textual interpretation.
4
Conclude the defense
With the genus interpretation, the definition reads: 'speech of Allah that relates to any one action of any legally responsible person'. This includes all rulings (general and specific) and excludes statements about Allah’s essence. Both defects are removed.
The definition is now comprehensive and inclusive of prophetic specificities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the meaning of its relation to the actions of the legally responsible persons... Purpose: answer to an anticipated question. Question: The definition of hukm is not comprehensive; it does not apply to any of its individuals because in 'relation to the actions of the legally responsible persons', both 'actions' and 'legally responsible persons' are plural. So the meaning would be that hukm is that speech of Allah which relates to all actions of all legally responsible persons. However, there is no such speech of Allah that relates to all actions of all legally responsible persons. Then two defects arise: (1) the definition would not be comprehensive, not applying to any individual of hukm; (2) the specific rulings for the Prophet would be excluded from the definition, e.g., the permissibility of marrying more than four is specific to the Prophet, so that speech relates only to one legally responsible person (the Prophet). Answer: The summary is that 'actions' is plural and is annexed to 'legally responsible persons', and that is also a plural defined by al. The rule is that when a plural is defined by al or is annexed to a plural defined by al, its plurality is nullified, and it becomes like a genus plural. So here, from the plural 'actions', the genus of action is meant, and from 'legally responsible persons', the genus of legally responsible person is meant. Thus, 'relation to the actions of the legally responsible persons' means: hukm is the speech of Allah that relates to any one action of the genus of legally responsible person. Now the definition is correct, and both defects are removed. The definition will be comprehensive of all individuals, and the specific rulings for the Prophet will also enter the definition because they relate to one legally responsible person (the Prophet). However, that speech of Allah that does not relate to any action of a legally responsible person is excluded from 'related to actions of the legally responsible persons', e.g., that speech of Allah that relates to His essence, attributes, and transcendences.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection to the definition of hukm as 'the speech of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible persons'. The objection is that the plurals imply it must relate to all actions of all responsible persons, which is impossible. The answer applies a rule of Arabic grammar: a plural defined by al or annexed to a plural defined by al indicates the genus, not the universal set. Thus the definition means any action of any responsible person, making it comprehensive. This defense ensures that even rulings specific to the Prophet (e.g., marrying more than four) are included, while statements about Allah's essence are excluded.

Key Terms
حکم (hukm): Allah's speech that relates to the actions of the legally responsible persons (by demand or option)
جمع معرف باللام (jam' mu'arraf bi al-lam): A plural noun defined by the definite article 'al', which according to Hanafi usul denotes genus, not universality

The Hanafi rule that a plural defined by 'al' denotes genus is a powerful interpretive tool that saves the definition of hukm from apparent contradiction.

The Definition of Hukm and the Objection Regarding the Prophet's Address
Defending that true hukm is only from Allah's address

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi definition of 'hukm' as Allah's address includes the Prophet's rulings, and defend this definition against the objection of non-comprehensiveness.

Core Idea
The Prophet's rulings are hukm only because Allah commanded obedience to him.

The definition of hukm as 'the address of Allah' seems to exclude the Prophet's statements, which are also called hukm and are binding. This objection challenges the comprehensiveness of the definition. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi response: the Prophet's address is subsumed under Allah's address because Allah commands obedience to the Prophet. Thus, the definition remains comprehensive and sound.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Identify the objection: if hukm is defined as Allah's address only, then how can we call the Prophet's statements 'hukm' and consider them obligatory? The objection claims the definition is not comprehensive.
The objection relies on common usage where 'hukm' is applied to the Prophet's words.
2
Examine the Hanafi definition
The definition uses 'idafah' (annexation) to specify that hukm is specifically Allah's address. This specification is deliberate to indicate ontological source.
Idafah here indicates that hukm originates from Allah alone.
3
Identify the apparent counterexample
The Prophet's address, obedience to those in authority, and a slave's obedience to his master are all called hukm and are obligatory. These seem to fall outside the definition.
The objection lists multiple categories of binding addresses.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The obligation to follow the Prophet, those in authority, and masters comes only because Allah commanded it. Their rulings derive authority from Allah's address.
Use Quranic evidence: 'Obey Allah and obey the Messenger' (4:59).
5
Confirm comprehensiveness
Since all binding rulings ultimately trace back to Allah's command, the definition 'Allah's address' includes them by extension. The definition is comprehensive.
The Prophet's address is not independent hukm; it is a manifestation of Allah's hukm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا یقال اضافة الخطاب الى الله تعالى الخ غرض اشکال و جواب سوال یہ ہوتا ہے کہ حکم کی تعریف خطاب اللہ کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے اور خطاب کی اضافت اللہ کی طرف ہے اور اضافت اختصاص مضاف بالمضاف الیہ کو مقتضی ہوتی ہے تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حکم صرف اللہ ہی کے خطاب کو کہا جاتا ہے اور صرف اسی کی اطاعت واجب ہے حالانکہ خطاب النبی کو بھی حکم کہا جاتا ہے اس کی اطاعت بھی واجب ہے اسی طرح اولی الامر کی اطاعت اور غلام کیلئے آقا کی اطاعت بھی واجب ہے ان سب کے خطاب کو بھی حکم کہا جاتا ہے لیکن حکم کی تعریف ان پر صادق نہیں آ رہی تو تعریف جامع نہ رہی۔ جواب : خلاصہ جواب یہ ہے کہ اضافت خطاب الی اللہ مفید اختصاص ہے اور یہ اختصاص بالکل صحیح ہے حکم صرف اللہ ہی کے خطاب کو کہا جاتا ہے باقی رہا اطاعت النبی وحکم النبی واطاعت اولی الامر وغیرہ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان کی اطاعت بھی بحکم اللہ و بخطاب اللہ و با یجاب اللہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی نے ان کی اطاعت کا حکم فرمایا ہے. اللہ تعالی اگر ان کی اطاعت کا حکم نہ فرماتے تو ان کی اطاعت بھی واجب نہ ہوتی اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ حقیقتا حکم صرف خطاب اللہ ہی کا نام ہے لہذا تعریف جامع ہے خطاب النبی وغیرہ خطاب اللہ میں داخل ہو جائینگے
It should not be said that the addition of address to Allah... Purpose: objection and answer. Question: The definition of hukm is given as the address of Allah, and the address is added to Allah, and addition requires specification of the added to the one to which it is added. So it is understood that hukm is only called the address of Allah, and only His obedience is obligatory. However, the address of the Prophet is also called hukm, and his obedience is obligatory. Similarly, obedience to those in authority and the obedience of a slave to his master is also obligatory. The addresses of all these are also called hukm, but the definition of hukm does not apply to them, so the definition is not comprehensive. Answer: The summary is that the addition of address to Allah indicates specification, and this specification is absolutely correct. Hukm is only called the address of Allah. As for obedience to the Prophet, the ruling of the Prophet, obedience to those in authority, etc., the answer is that their obedience is also by the command of Allah, by the address of Allah, and by the obligation of Allah. Allah has commanded their obedience. If Allah had not commanded their obedience, their obedience would not be obligatory. This proves that in reality, hukm is only the name of the address of Allah. Therefore, the definition is comprehensive; the address of the Prophet etc. are included in the address of Allah.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection: if hukm is only Allah's address, then how can we call the Prophet's statements 'hukm' and consider them binding? The answer is that the Prophet's rulings are binding because Allah commanded us to obey him. Hence, the true source of obligation is Allah's address; the Prophet's address is a manifestation of that. Thus, the definition remains comprehensive, as all binding statements ultimately derive from Allah's address.

Key Terms
اضافت (idafah): Grammatical addition/annexation indicating specification of the added to the addressee
حكم (hukm): In Hanafi usul: the address of Allah pertaining to the actions of the legally responsible (mukallaf).
خطاب (khitab): Address or speech directed to someone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm as Allah's address remains comprehensive because all binding commands ultimately derive from His command.

Refining the Definition of Hukm: Adding the Condition of Demand or Option
Adding the condition of demand or option to exclude stories and reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi definition of hukm requires the condition of iqtida' or takhyir, and identify which types of speech are excluded.

Core Idea
A hukm demands action or grants choice; mere stories about actions are not hukm.

In this passage, we encounter a critical objection to the definition of hukm as 'Allah's speech related to the actions of the legally responsible persons.' If taken literally, this definition would include Quranic stories and reports that describe actions without imposing any obligation or giving permission. The Hanafi response is to qualify the definition with the condition of iqtida' (demand) or takhyir (option). This refinement ensures that only speech that directs human action—whether by commanding, prohibiting, recommending, disapproving, or permitting—qualifies as hukm. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The definition of hukm as 'Allah's speech related to actions' is too broad because it includes Quranic stories and reports about actions, which are not considered hukm.
The objection is about exclusiveness (ghayr mani').
2
Understand why stories are not hukm
Stories and reports merely inform about actions without imposing any demand or giving a choice. They lack the directive nature of hukm.
Example: 'And Allah created you and what you do' (al-Saffat:96) is an informative report, not a legal ruling.
3
Learn the refinement
The solution is to add the condition 'by demand (iqtida') or option (takhyir)' to the definition. This excludes all purely informative speech.
The refined definition: 'Allah's speech that involves a demand or option regarding the actions of the legally responsible persons.'
4
Define iqtida' and takhyir
Iqtida' is a demand for action or abstinence, covering: obligation (action required, leaving prohibited), recommendation (action encouraged but not required), prohibition (leaving required, action prohibited), and disapproval (leaving encouraged but not required). Takhyir is granting the choice to do or leave (permissibility).
These five categories are the ahkam al-khamsah.
5
Confirm exclusivity
Stories and reports contain neither demand nor option; they are purely informative. Thus, they are excluded from the definition, making it exclusive.

ثم اعترض على هذا التعريف بانه غیر مانع الخ گذشته اعتراض جامعیت پر وارد تھا یہ اعتراض ! مانعیت پر ہے کہ حکم کی تعریف خطاب اللہ مانع نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ قصص جو مکلفین کے احوال بیان کر رہے ہیں اور وہ اخبار جو مکلفین کے اعمال سے متعلق ہیں مثلاً والله خلقكم وما تعملون یہ ایک خبر ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہیں اور تمہارے اعمال کو پیدا فرمایا تو یہ بھی ایک خطاب ہے جس کا تعلق اعمال و افعال مکلفین کے ساتھ بصورت خبر ہے تو یہ دونوں تعریف حکم میں داخل ہورہے ہیں حالانکہ ان کو حکم نہیں کہا جاتا ۔ جواب ! اس کے دو جواب دیے گئے ہیں بعض حضرات نے یہ جواب دیا ہے کہ حکم کی تعریف میں ہم بالاقتضاء او الخجیر کی قید لگادیں گے تو یہ اعتراض دفع ہو جائے گا اور تعریف مانع ہو جائے گی کیونکہ خطاب اللہ کا تعلق افعال کے ساتھ نقص میں اسی طرح خطاب کا تعلق اعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ اخبار میں ، یہ اقتضاء اور تخیر والا تعلق نہیں ہے ان میں نہ اقتضاء ہے اور نہ ہی تخییر کیونکہ تخیر کا معنی ہے مکلف کو فعل و ترک دونوں کا اختیار دے دیا جائے اور اقتضاء کا معنی ہے مکلف سے فعل کا مطالبہ کیا جائے اور ترک سے منع ہو اس کو ایجاب کہتے ہیں یا فعل کا مطالبہ ہو لیکن ترک سے ممانعت نہ ہو اس کو ندب کہتے ہیں، یا ترک فعل کا مطالبہ ہو اور فعل سے ممانعت ہو اس کو تحریم کہتے ہیں، یا ترک کا مطالبہ ہو لیکن فعل سے منع نہ ہو اس کو کراہت کہتے ہیں اور یہ تمام اقسام ان نقص و اخبار میں نہیں پائی جاتیں جو افعال مکلفین کے احوال کو بیان کرتی ہیں لہذا یہ دونوں
Then objection was raised against this definition that it is not exclusive... Previous objection was on comprehensiveness; this objection is on exclusiveness: the definition of hukm as speech of Allah is not exclusive because the stories that narrate the conditions of the legally responsible persons and the reports related to their actions, e.g., 'And Allah created you and what you do' – this is a report that Allah created you and your deeds. This too is an address related to the actions of the legally responsible persons in the form of news. So both of these enter the definition of hukm, although they are not called hukm. Answer: Two answers have been given. Some scholars said we will add the condition of 'by demand or option' in the definition of hukm, then this objection will be repelled and the definition will be exclusive. Because the relation of Allah's address to actions in demand is such that the address relates to the actions of the legally responsible persons in the form of news; this is not a demand or option relation. In them there is neither demand nor option. Because option means giving the legally responsible person the choice to do or leave; demand means requiring the action and prohibiting leaving – that is called obligation; or requiring the action but not prohibiting leaving – that is called recommendation; or requiring leaving the action and prohibiting doing – that is called prohibition; or requiring leaving but not prohibiting doing – that is called disapproval. All these types are not found in those stories and reports that describe the conditions of the actions of the legally responsible persons. Therefore, both of these [are excluded].
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage addresses a different objection: the definition of hukm as 'Allah's speech related to actions' is too broad; it includes Quranic stories and reports about the actions of people, which are not hukm. The solution is to add the condition that the speech must involve a demand (iqtida') or option (takhyir). Demand includes obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and disapproval. Option is the permissibility category. Stories and reports merely inform without imposing any demand or giving an option, so they are excluded. This refinement makes the definition both comprehensive and exclusive.

Key Terms
اقتضاء (iqtida'): Demand for action or abstinence, covering obligation, recommendation, prohibition, and disapproval
تخییر (takhyir): Giving the choice to do or not do (permissibility)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition is added to the definition of hukm to exclude Quranic stories about actions?
A) The speech must be eternal
B) The speech must involve a demand or option
C) The speech must be in Arabic
D) The speech must be revealed to the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm is refined to include only speech that demands action or grants choice, excluding informative stories.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Three Mu'tazila Objections to the Definition of Hukm
Dispute on definition of hukm with Mu'tazila objections and Ash'ari responses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Mu'tazila objections to the Ash'ari/Hanafi definition of hukm and explain the Ash'ari responses, identifying the key distinction between the essence and relation of a ruling.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila confuse the eternal essence of hukm with its contingent relation; Ash'aris affirm both.

The definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah' is foundational in Hanafi usul. The Mu'tazila raised three objections, arguing that hukm is contingent, that the word 'aw' introduces doubt, and that the definition excludes wad'i rulings. This lesson examines each objection and the Ash'ari responses, which the Hanafi school adopts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Definition
Recall the definition of hukm as 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi fi'il al-mukallaf bi al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir aw al-wad''. This is the Ash'ari/Hanafi position.
2
First Objection: Contingency vs Eternity
Mu'tazila argue hukm is contingent (hadith) because it occurs after non-existence and is caused by contingent causes, while khitab is eternal (qadim). Thus defining contingent by eternal is invalid.
The Ash'ari response distinguishes essence (eternal) from relation (contingent).
3
Second Objection: The Word 'Aw'
Mu'tazila claim 'aw' in the definition introduces doubt, which contradicts the purpose of definition. Ash'aris respond that 'aw' here is for disjunction (taqsim), not doubt.
4
Third Objection: Not Comprehensive
Mu'tazila object that the definition covers only taklifi rulings, not wad'i (sabab, shart, mani'). Ash'aris respond by adding 'aw al-wad'' to include them.
The author (Sadr al-Shariah) includes this in the matn.
5
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: if hukm is contingent, rulings are created at the time of action; if eternal, they are part of God's eternal knowledge, affecting how we understand the Quran as eternal speech.

ساتھ تو نفس حکم مسبوق بالعدم اور متصف بالعدم نہیں ہوتا البتہ تعلق حکم بالشئی یہ حادث اور متصف بالحصول بعد العدم ہوتا ہے اور اعتراض میں جو مثال دی گئی تھی حلت المرنة تو اس کا مطلب بھی یہی ہے کہ عورت کے ساتھ پہلے حالت کا تعلق نہیں تھا بعد میں نکاح کی وجہ سے حالت کا تعلق اس کے نہاتھ ہو گیا ہے یہ مطلب نہیں کہ نفس حالت پہلے نہیں تھی بعد میں وجود میں آئی بلکہ نفس حالت تو ازل وابد سے موجود تھی البتہ اس عورت کے ساتھ اس کا
Misk al-Malih: Commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. (Stories and news) will be excluded from the definition of hukm. And some have responded that the second answer is that there is no need to restrict with 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir' to prevent the definition from including stories and news; rather, the restriction here is by 'haythiyya', meaning 'the address of Allah pertaining to the act of the mukallaf insofar as it is the act of the mukallaf.' The purpose is that hukm is the address that relates to the acts of the mukallaf in terms of being acts of the mukallaf. And the address of Allah relates to stories and news not as acts of the mukallaf, but as matters emanating from existents, i.e., as existent and occurred affairs. So they are not included in the definition. The author said: 'Some added.' The Mu'tazila objected to this definition with three aspects. The commentator of al-Tawdih states that the Ash'aris defined hukm as 'khitab Allah' and the Mu'tazila objected on three grounds. The author mentioned only one objection and gave the Ash'ari response, which is the restriction with 'aw al-wad'' to include al-hukm al-wad'i. The remaining two objections the author did not mention in the text. The commentator al-Taftazani details the three objections and gives their responses. First objection: 'Indeed, the address with you is eternal...' The first objection from the Mu'tazila is that you define hukm as khitab Allah, and according to you, khitab is eternal (since khitab means kalam nafsi, which is eternal), while hukm is contingent. So the definiendum (hukm) is contingent, and its definition (khitab Allah) is eternal, necessitating defining the contingent by the eternal, which is invalid because defining a thing by its opposite is not permissible. Question: Why is hukm contingent? The commentator gives two proofs for the contingency of hukm: (1) Hukm is characterized by occurrence after non-existence; it is preceded by non-existence. He gives the example of 'hillat al-mar'a' (permissibility of marriage). (2) Hukm is caused by a contingent cause. So since causes are contingent, their effects (hukm) are contingent. Thus hukm is contingent. Second objection: Your definition contains the word 'aw' (or) with 'bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir'. The rule is that in definitions, mentioning 'aw' is problematic because 'aw' is placed for doubt and hesitation. If used in a definition, it creates doubt and ambiguity, whereas definition is meant to clarify. So 'aw' contradicts definition. Third objection: 'It is not comprehensive.' The Mu'tazila object that the definition is not comprehensive because there are two types of hukm: taklifi and wad'i. This definition covers taklifi but not wad'i, as wad'i does not involve either iqtida' or takhyir. Examples: causality (sababiyya) of the sun for obligation of zuhr prayer, conditionality (shartiyya) of wudu for prayer, preventive (mani'yya) of menstruation for prayer. After presenting the three objections, the commentator al-Taftazani criticizes the author for omitting some aspects. Then the Ash'ari responses: First objection response: According to us, hukm is also eternal, so it is definition of eternal by eternal. As for the two proofs of contingency, we respond: Hukm has two aspects: the essence of the ruling (nafs al-hukm) and its relation (ta'alliq) to something. The essence is not preceded by non-existence, only the relation is contingent. The example of 'hillat al-mar'a' means the relation of permissibility to the woman was not present before, not the essence of permissibility, which is eternal.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
The passage begins with a continuation of discussion on the definition of hukm (ruling) as 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi fi'il al-mukallaf' (the address of Allah pertaining to the act of the legally responsible person). The commentator al-Taftazani clarifies a point about stories and news (qisas wa akhbar) that are excluded from the definition because they pertain to acts that have already occurred, not as acts of the mukallaf. The main part of the passage deals with three objections by the Mu'tazila against the Ash'ari definition of hukm. The first objection is that hukm is contingent (hadith) while khitab (meaning kalam nafsi) is eternal (qadim), so defining a contingent thing by an eternal one is invalid. The Mu'tazila provide two proofs for contingency: (a) hukm occurs after non-existence (e.g., permissibility of marriage after nikkah), and (b) hukm is caused by a contingent cause (e.g., permissibility caused by marriage). The second objection concerns the use of the word 'aw' (or) in the definition (bi-al-iqtida' aw al-takhyir), arguing that 'aw' introduces doubt, which is inappropriate for a definition meant to clarify. The third objection is that the definition is not comprehensive (ghayr jami') because it only covers taklifi rulings and not wad'i rulings (like sababiyya, shartiyya, mani'yya). The commentator then notes that the author (Sadr al-Shariah) omitted two of these objections in the matn, but al-Taftazani includes them. After presenting the objections, al-Taftazani gives the Ash'ari responses. The response to the first objection is that hukm is also eternal; the apparent contingency is only in the relation (ta'alliq) of the ruling to specific acts, not in the essence (nafs) of the ruling. The essence of permissibility (hillah) is eternal, but its connection to a particular woman occurs after nikkah. The response to the second objection is that 'aw' here is not for doubt but for disjunction (takhayur) to encompass different types of rulings (iqtida'i and takhyiri). The Ash'aris may also argue that the definition is comprehensive because the word 'aw' is used for division (taqsim). For the third objection, the Ash'aris respond by adding the phrase 'aw al-wad'' (or al-wad'i) to the definition, as the author did, to include wad'i rulings. Thus the definition becomes comprehensive. The passage ends with a side note that the commentator criticizes the author for omitting 'mani'yya' in the examples of wad'i rulings, but it is excused since the purpose was only to give examples.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The address of Allah pertaining to the act of the mukallaf, including both taklifi and wad'i rulings.
خطاب الله (khitab Allah): The eternal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah, the source of all rulings.
حدوث (huduth): Contingency or originatedness; the quality of coming into existence after non-existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the central distinction in the Ash'ari response to the first Mu'tazila objection?
A) Hukm is created; khitab is created.
B) The essence of hukm is eternal, only its relation to acts is contingent.
C) Hukm is contingent because of its cause, but the definition is still valid.
D) The definition is changed to avoid contingency.

Key Takeaway
The three Mu'tazila objections are answered by the Ash'ari distinction between essence and relation, the functional use of 'aw', and the inclusion of wad'i rulings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Refuting Mu'tazila on the Eternity of Hukm
Ash'ari response to Mu'tazila objections on the definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi/Ash'ari school holds that hukm is qadim and refute the Mu'tazila objections using the distinction between essence and relation and between efficient and epistemic cause.

Core Idea
Hukm's essence is eternal; only its relation to temporal events changes.

This passage presents the Ash'ari response to Mu'tazila objections against the definition of hukm as Allah's discourse. The Mu'tazila argued that hukm must be temporal because it relates to temporal events and is caused by them. The Ash'ari reply distinguishes between the eternal essence of hukm and its temporal relation to specific events, and between efficient causes that produce effects and epistemic causes that merely indicate an eternal ruling. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the Hanafi position on divine attributes and legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Mu'tazila objections
From the passage, extract each objection: 1) hukm is temporal, so defining it as Allah's discourse is circular; 2) the word 'aw' in the definition causes doubt; 3) the definition does not cover wad'i rulings.
The third objection is briefly addressed; focus on the first two.
2
Analyze the first objection and its refutation
The Mu'tazila gave two proofs: (a) hukm is characterized by existence after non-existence, and (b) hukm is caused by temporal causes. The Ash'ari response: the essence of hukm is eternal; only its relation (ta'alluq) to events is temporal. The cause is epistemic, not efficient, so a temporal cause does not necessitate a temporal effect.
Note the key terms: illa mu'aththira vs. illa mu'arrafa.
3
Analyze the second objection and its refutation
The Mu'tazila claim 'aw' in definitions creates doubt. The Ash'ari response distinguishes 'aw tawzi'iyya' (for division) from 'aw tashkikiyya' (for doubt). Here 'aw' is tawzi'iyya, so it is permissible.
This distinction is standard in usul al-fiqh.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If hukm were temporal, abrogation would mean the ruling ceases to exist. Because it is eternal, abrogation only changes its manifestation. For example, the eternal ruling that wine is haram remains; its application to a specific instance is temporal.
This ties theological debate to fiqh.

It is pre-eternal, therefore defining hukm as Allah's discourse is not correct. Second objection! From the Mu'tazila it is made that your definition includes the word 'aw' (or) by requirement or choice, and the rule is that in definitions, the mention of 'aw' is problematic because it is used for doubt and confusion. If it is mentioned in the definition, it will create doubt and ambiguity, while the definition is for clarification and specification. So mentioning 'aw' is against definition. Third objection! That it is not comprehensive. The Mu'tazila object to the Ash'ari that the definition of hukm is not comprehensive because there are two types: taklifi and wad'i. This definition includes taklifi but does not apply to wad'i, which includes cause, condition, and preventer. The author omitted mention of preventer. The commentator responds by saying that 'and the like' covers it, or the intention was just to give examples. Then the Ash'ari response to the three objections: first objection: Mu'tazila claim hukm is temporal, but Ash'ari say it is eternal like the discourse itself. They refute the two proofs: (1) hukm being characterized by existence after non-existence refers to the relation, not the essence. (2) The cause of hukm is an epistemic cause, not an efficient one; temporal causes indicate the eternal ruling without causing it. Thus both proofs fail, and the eternity of hukm is established. Then the second objection about 'aw': it is answered by distinguishing 'aw tawzi'iyya' (for division) and 'aw tashkikiyya' (for doubt). Here it is tawzi'iyya, so permissible.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents the Ash'ari responses to three objections from the Mu'tazila against the definition of hukm (as 'Allah's discourse relating to the actions of the obligated, by requirement or choice'). The first objection is that hukm is temporal, so defining it as eternal is circular. The Ash'ari respond by distinguishing between the essence of hukm (eternal) and its relation to specific events (temporal). They refute the Mu'tazila's two proofs: (1) existence after non-existence applies only to the relation, not the essence; (2) the cause of hukm is an epistemic cause, not an efficient one—temporal acts merely indicate the eternal ruling. The second objection is about the word 'aw' in the definition causing doubt. The response is that 'aw' is of two types: tawzi'iyya (for dividing types, permissible) and tashkikiyya (for doubt, forbidden). Here it is tawzi'iyya. The third objection about comprehensiveness is briefly addressed by noting the author's intent was to give examples, not list all types. The passage ends while discussing the second objection in detail.

Key Terms
حکم (hukm): The divine ruling (khattab Allah) relating to the actions of the obligated, by requirement or choice.
او تنویعیہ (aw tawzi'iyya): The word 'or' used for dividing types and specifying the aspects of a defined thing.
او تشکیکیہ (aw tashkikiyya): The word 'or' used to express doubt or to cast the addressee into uncertainty.
علت مؤثرہ (illa mu'aththira): An efficient cause that brings about the existence of the effect and upon which the effect depends.
علت معرفہ (illa mu'arrafa): An epistemic cause that acts only as a sign or indicator of the ruling, without being efficient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari response, what is the reason that the word 'aw' in the definition of hukm is permissible?
A) It is used for tashkik (doubt)
B) It is used for tawzi' (division)
C) It is used for takhyir (choice)
D) It is used for taqsim (classification)

Key Takeaway
The eternity of hukm in Ash'ari/Hanafi thought is preserved by distinguishing between the ruling's essence and its relation to temporal events, and by classifying legal causes as epistemic signs rather than efficient causes.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
The Definition of Hukm: Must Wad'i Rulings Be Explicitly Included?
Response to third objection of Mu'tazila and Ash'ari factions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Ash'ari positions on including wad'i rulings in the definition of hukm and evaluate the Hanafi preference for explicit inclusion.

Core Idea
Taklifi and wad'i are mutually exclusive concepts; their mutual entailment does not justify subsuming one under the other.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: how should the definition of 'hukm' (legal ruling) encompass both taklifi and wad'i rulings? The Mu'tazila objected that the standard Ash'ari definition excluded wad'i rulings. The Ash'ari response split into three groups. The Hanafi school, following the author of the matn, endorses explicit inclusion. We will trace the arguments and understand why conceptual distinctness matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The Mu'tazila objected that the definition of hukm (as 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin bi'l-iqtida' aw al-takhyir') excludes wad'i rulings (sabab, shart, mani).
2
Distinguish the three Ash'ari groups
First group: add 'aw al-wad'' explicitly. Second group: deny wad'i as hukm entirely. Third group: subsume wad'i under iqtida' dhimni (implicit demand).
The commentator Taftazani mistakenly merged the second and third groups.
3
Analyze the third group's subsumption argument
They argue that wad'i rulings entail taklifi consequences (obligation/prohibition), so they fall under iqtida' (which includes both explicit and implicit).
Example: sababiyyat duluk entails obligation of prayer.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
Taklifi and wad'i are mutabayinan (mutually exclusive in concept). Entailment (talazum) does not prove identity; distinct entities can entail each other.
Hanafis reject subsumption because it conflates conceptual categories.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The author of the matn (Sadr al-Shari'ah) prefers the second group's addition of 'aw al-wad''. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
The definition becomes: 'khitab Allah ... bi'l-iqtida' aw al-takhyir aw al-wad''.

دونوں کا تلازم اور ایک دوسرے کو لازم ہونا ان کے اتحاد پر دلالت نہیں کرتا مثلا سبیت دلوک کا وجوب صلوۃ وستلزم ہونا وغیرہ تلازم کبھی دو متباینان کے درمیان بھی ہو جاتا ہے فتفکر ۔ تبصرہ ! شارح تفتازانی نے کو بھی فریق ثانی کی طرف منسوب کر دیا ہے حالانکہ یہ غلط ہے بلکہ یہ جواب اشاعرہ کے ایک اور گروہ کی جانب سے ہے حقیقت یہ ہے کہ اعتراض ثالث کے جواب میں اشاعرہ کے دو گروہ نہیں بلکہ تین ہیں (۱) فریق اول ، وہ ہے جس نے اشکال معتزلہ تسلیم کر کے او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کر دیا ہے (۲) فریق ثانی ، وہ ہے جو خطاب وضع کو حکم ہی تسلیم نہیں کرتا اور نہ او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کرتا ہے (۳) فریق ثالث ، وہ ہے جو خطاب ملاحظہ فرمائیے ان الاشاعرة في هذا المقام ثلاث فرق منهم من لم يسم الوضعى حكما ومنهم من سماه حكما وزاد قيد الوضع ومنهم من سماه حكما وادرجه فيه بجعل الاقتضاء اعم من الصريحي والضمنی مصنف نے فرق ثلاثہ میں سے فرقہ اولی کو جو خطاب وضعی کو حکم تسلیم نہیں کرتا اپنے متن میں ذکر ہی نہیں کیا اور فرقہ ثانیہ جو او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کرتا ہے اس کو مختار اور حق قرار دیا اور فرقہ ثالثہ جو خطاب وضعی کو الاقتضاء میں درج کرتا تھا اس کی رائے کو ناحق قرار دے کر مستر د کر
There were types and categories: sometimes the ruling relates to the action of the obligated person with iqtida' and demand, sometimes with non-obligatory choice, sometimes it is a taklifi ruling, sometimes a wad'i ruling. So it was impossible to combine these different types and categories of ruling into one limit and definition without mentioning detail and 'aw'. Therefore, 'aw' is mentioned here for the purpose of dividing into types and limited detail, so this 'aw' is of division (tawzi'iyya) and its mention in the definition is permissible and good. As for the third [objection], some took it up: the commentator is responding to the third objection of the Ash'aris. Thus he said: To answer the third objection, the Ash'aris divided into two groups (according to the commentator Taftazani, rather there are three groups). The first group replied: We concede that this definition does not include wad'i rulings, so it is not comprehensive; your objection is valid. Therefore, to make this definition comprehensive, we add the qayd (restriction) 'aw al-wad'' so that this definition includes wad'i rulings and becomes comprehensive (jam' al-afrad). According to this group, the definition of hukm is: 'The address of Allah the Exalted related to the actions of the obligated persons by iqtida' or takhyir or wad''. (2) The second group gave two answers (according to the commentator): one answer of non-acceptance, the second answer of acceptance. The answer of non-acceptance is: O Mu'tazili, we do not accept at all that wad'i address is a ruling. Rather, ruling has only one type: taklifi address. Therefore, since wad'i address is not a ruling, there is no need to add any restriction to include it in the definition; rather, it should remain excluded from the definition. And if someone insists on calling this wad'i address a ruling, that is his choice; we in any case do not call it a ruling. For us, up to 'aw al-takhyir' the definition is complete and perfect; there is no need for the qayd 'aw al-wad''. Whoever says wad'i address is a ruling must change the definition; it is not necessary upon us. 'wa law sallamna' (even if we concede): from this, the second group's second answer of acceptance is mentioned: If we hypothetically concede that wad'i address is included in ruling, still your objection that the definition is not comprehensive and does not include wad'i ruling, therefore the qayd 'aw al-wad'' should be there, is wrong. Rather, the definition is still comprehensive; it includes both types (taklifi and wad'i) of ruling; there is no need to add the qayd 'aw al-wad''. Because in the definition of hukm, the word iqtida' and takhyir are mentioned. Iqtida' has two forms: (1) explicit (sarihi) (2) implicit (dhimni). And iqtida' is divided; it includes both explicit and implicit. And in wad'i address, there is implicit iqtida' (iqtida' dhimni). Therefore, this too enters under iqtida' and enters the definition of hukm, and the definition becomes comprehensive. Question: How is there implicit iqtida' in wad'i address? Answer: Implicit iqtida' in wad'i address is like this: For example, 'sababiyyat duluk al-shams' is a wad'i address; its meaning is that at the time of declining sun, prayer is obligatory. Similarly, 'shartiyyat al-tahara' is a wad'i ruling; its meaning is that purification in prayer is obligatory, or prayer without purification is forbidden. 'Mani'iyyat al-najasa 'an al-salat' is a wad'i ruling; its purpose is that performing prayer while impurity exists is forbidden, or removing impurity during prayer is obligatory. From this, it is proven that in the three instances of wad'i address - sababiyya, shartiyya, mani'iyya - there is iqtida', though not explicit, but implicit iqtida' exists. Because the result of these three is obligation and prohibition, which are among the individual instances of iqtida'. Similarly, all causes, conditions, and preventers can be interpreted and entered under implicit iqtida'. Therefore, there is no need for any additional restriction for wad'i rulings. 'wa dhahaba al-musannif' - the commentator explains the author's opinion: The author has gone to the view that the truth is that in the definition of hukm, the qayd 'aw al-wad'' should be added. Because when there are two types of address - taklifi and wad'i - and one is mentioned, the other type should also be mentioned so that the definition is comprehensive. And the author also said that entering wad'i address under iqtida' or takhyir (i.e., into taklifi address) is not correct. The reason he gave is that these two (taklifi and wad'i) are different in concept (mutaghayir al-mafhum) and mutually exclusive (mutabayinan) in terms of meaning. Entering one mutually exclusive into another is not correct; rather, each must be mentioned independently. And in some cases, the entailment (talazum) of these two and their being necessary for each other does not indicate their unity. For example, the entailment of sababiyyat duluk with obligation of prayer, etc. Entailment sometimes occurs between two mutually exclusive things. So reflect. Commentary! The commentator Taftazani made two groups of Ash'aris in answering the third objection: the first group is those who accept the objection and add the qayd 'aw al-wad''; and the commentator transmitted two answers from the second group: the first answer is non-acceptance - that they do not at all accept wad'i address as a ruling; the second answer of the same second group is acceptance - that if we accept wad'i address as a ruling, the qayd 'aw al-wad'' is not necessary; rather, wad'i address is included under implicit iqtida'. So the commentator attributed this answer also to the second group, but this is incorrect. Rather, this answer is from another group of Ash'aris. The reality is that in answering the third objection, the Ash'aris are not two groups but three: (1) The first group: those who accepted the Mu'tazilite objection and added the qayd 'aw al-wad''. (2) The second group: those who do not accept wad'i address as a ruling at all and do not add the qayd 'aw al-wad''. (3) The third group: those who accept that wad'i address is a ruling but do not accept the addition of the qayd 'aw al-wad''; rather, they expand iqtida' and enter wad'i address under implicit iqtida'. See the statement of 'Allama 'Adud al-Din in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Usul: 'Indeed the Ash'aris in this context are three sects: among them are those who did not call wad'i a ruling; among them are those who called it a ruling and added the qayd al-wad'; and among them are those who called it a ruling and entered it into the definition by making iqtida' more general than explicit and implicit.' The author, from the three sects, did not mention in his text the first sect (those who do not accept wad'i as a ruling); he chose and declared as true the second sect (those who add the qayd 'aw al-wad''); and he declared false and rejected the opinion of the third sect (those who entered wad'i address under iqtida').
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute over the proper definition of 'hukm' (legal ruling). The issue arises from an objection by the Mu'tazila that the standard Ash'ari definition (limited to taklifi rulings) fails to include wad'i rulings (e.g., cause, condition, preventer). The text first explains that the word 'aw' (or) in the definition is used for division (tawzi') not ambiguity, making it permissible. Then it details the Ash'ari response, which the commentator Taftazani mistakenly splits into two groups; the author corrects this to three: (1) those who add 'aw al-wad'' explicitly, (2) those who deny wad'i as a ruling altogether, and (3) those who subsume wad'i under 'iqtida' dhimni' (implicit demand). The author, following the matn of Sadr al-Shari'ah, endorses the first group and rejects the third, arguing that taklifi and wad'i are mutually exclusive concepts (mutabayinan) and that entailment does not imply identity. Examples from prayer (sababiyyat duluk, shartiyyat tahara, mani'iyyat najasa) illustrate how wad'i rulings entail obligations/prohibitions but remain conceptually distinct. The Hanafi position aligns with the first group: the definition must explicitly include wad'i rulings by adding 'aw al-wad''.

Key Terms
حكم تكليفي (hukm taklifi): Ruling that directly demands or gives choice regarding an action, e.g., wajib, haram, mandub.
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): Ruling that establishes a thing as a cause, condition, or preventer, e.g., sabab, shart, mani.
اقتضاء ضمني (iqtida' dhimni): Implicit demand inferred from the legal effect of a wad'i ruling.
اقتضاء صريحي (iqtida' sarihi): Explicit demand, as in direct commands and prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of the matn, which Ash'ari group's position is correct regarding the definition of hukm?
A) The first group that rejects wad'i as a ruling altogether
B) The second group that adds 'aw al-wad'' to the definition
C) The third group that subsumes wad'i under iqtida' dhimni
D) The Mu'tazila position

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm must explicitly cover both taklifi and wad'i rulings because they are conceptually distinct, even though wad'i rules entail taklifi consequences.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
Definition of Hukm: Including Wad'i and the Three Ash'ari Groups
Critical refinement of the definition of hukm and the Ash'ari positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Ash'ari positions on including wad'i hukm in the definition of hukm and evaluate the Hanafi preference for adding 'aw al-wad''.

Core Idea
The definition of hukm must explicitly include wad'i rulings to avoid confusion between distinct categories.

In usul al-fiqh, precision in defining 'hukm' (legal ruling) is foundational. This passage examines a debate over whether the definition must include the phrase 'aw al-wad'' (or positing) to encompass wad'i rulings such as causes, conditions, and preventers. The author defends the necessity of this addition against Taftazani's objections, clarifying that there are three Ash'ari groups, not two. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to classify rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the debate
The passage asks whether the definition of hukm should explicitly include wad'i rulings or if they can be subsumed under iqtida' in taklifi.
2
Distinguish the three Ash'ari groups
List the three positions: (1) wad'i is not hukm; (2) wad'i is hukm and requires 'aw al-wad''; (3) wad'i is hukm but is included in an expanded iqtida'.
Taftazani incorrectly collapsed groups 1 and 3.
3
Analyze the Hanafi position
The author supports group 2: taklifi and wad'i are mutually exclusive in meaning, so each must be mentioned separately.
Hanafi usul traditionally adopts this view.
4
Critique Taftazani's error
Taftazani's objections are based on conflating groups 1 and 3; once corrected, his arguments dissolve.
5
Apply the definition
The practical consequence: the Hanafi definition of hukm includes both taklifi and wad'i explicitly via 'aw al-wad''.
This ensures comprehensiveness and prevents exclusion of valid rulings.

الصريحي والضمنی مصنف نے فرق ثلاثہ میں سے فرقہ اولی کو جو خطاب وضعی کو حکم تسلیم نہیں کرتا اپنے متن میں ذکر ہی نہیں کیا اور فرقہ ثانیہ جو او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کرتا ہے اس کو مختار اور حق قرار دیا اور فرقہ ثالثہ جو خطاب وضعی کو الاقتضاء میں درج کرتا تھا اس کی رائے کو ناحق قرار دے کر مستر د کر دیا اور شارح نے فرقہ اولى من لم يسم الوضع حكما ) اور فرقہ ثالث ( من سماه حكما وادرجه في الاقتضاء ) کو ایک ہی گروہ قرار دیدیا یہ اس سے نخش غلطی ہوئی اور مابعد وانست خبیر سے مصنف پر شارح تفتازانی جو اعتراضات کا قراردید سلسلہ شروع کر رہے ہیں وہ سب خود شارح تفتازانی کی غلط فہمی پرمبنی ہیں ورنہ اس حقیقت کے اضافہ ہونا چاہیئے ) غلط محض ہے اس کی اصلاح کی کوئی توجیہ نہیں ہو سکتی اما اولا سے پہلا اشکال ہے کہ مصنف کا یہ کہنا کہ حق یہ ہے او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ ہونا چاہئے تا که حکم وضعی تعریف حکم میں داخل ہو جائے درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ خصم (اشاعرہ) خطاب وضعی کو حکم تسلیم کرنے کیلئے تیا رہی نہیں ہے اور وہ صرف خطاب تکلیفی ہی کو حکم کہتے ہیں تو اس کیلئے تعریف حکم میں او الوضع کی قید لگانا کیسے واجب اور کیسے صحیح ہے بلکہ اس کیلئے تو اوالوضع کی قید نہ لگانا واجب ہے تا کہ یہ باہر ہی رہے اور تعریف حکم مانع عن دخول الغیر ہو ۔ جواب ! شارح تفتازانی کے اعتراض کا جواب یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ جناب عالی ہم ابھی وضاحت کر چکے ہیں کہ اشاعرہ کے تین گروہ ہیں (۱) گروہ وہ ہے جو ۔ خطاب وضعی کو حکم تسلیم نہیں کرتا اس گروہ کا مصنف نے اپنے متن میں سرے سے ذکر ہی نہیں کیا نہ ان پر رد کیا ہے نہ ان کی کلام کی توجیہ کی ہے مصنف نے تو ان دو گروہ کے بارے میں اپنی رائے پیش کی ہے جو خطاب وضعی کو حکم تسلیم کرتے ہیں پھر ایک گروہ او الوضع کی قید لگاتا ہے دوسرا اس کی ضرورت محسوس نہیں کرتا بلکہ اس کو اقتضا ضمنی میں داخل کرتا ہے مصنف نے ان کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ حق یہ ہے کہ او الوضع کی قید لگائی جائے الاقتضاء میں داخل نہ کیا جائے باقی جو خصم اس کو حکم تسلیم نہیں کرتا مصنف نے ان کے بارے میں کوئی بات ہی نہیں کی لہذا شارح کا اعتراض کہ مخصم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتا لغو اور باطل ہے ۔ واما ثانیا دوسرا اشکال یہ ہے کہ اگر شخصم (اشاعرہ ) اس خطاب وضعی کو حکم مان بھی لے تب بھی وہ ادا لوضع کی قید کی ضرورت محسوس نہیں کرتا بلکہ وہ کہتا ہے کہ یہ حکم کی تعریف میں ( بلا قید اوالوضع ) داخل ہے اس سے خارج نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ خطاب تکلیفی کی تعریف میں الاقتضاء کو اہم قرار دیتا ہے وہ خطاب تکلیفی اور وضعی دونوں کو شامل ہو جائے گا لہذا تب بھی او الوضع کی قید لگانا ضروری نہیں ہے باقی رہی مصنف کی یہ وجہ کہ یہ دونوں متغایر المفہوم ہیں لہذا دونوں کو علیحدہ ذکر کرنا چاہئے ، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ دونوں مفہوم کے اعتبار سے متغایر ہیں کیونکہ حکم تکلیفی عام اور حکم وضعی خاص ہے اور عام خاص آپس میں متغایرہ ہوتے ہیں۔ لیکن ان کے متغایر المفہوم ہونے سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ ان دونوں کو مستقل علیحدہ علیحدہ ذکر کیا جائے بلکہ یہ ایک دوسرے میں داخل ہو سکتے ہیں اس طرح کہ اقتضاء کو عام قرار دیا جائے وہ صریح اور ضمنی دونوں کو شامل ہو تو ان دونوں کا متغایر المنہو م ہونا ان کے تداخل میں مصر نہیں ہے جس طرح عام خاص متغاير المفہوم ہیں لیکن خاص عام میں داخل ہوتا ہے
Prayer is obligatory; from this it is proven that the three aspects of wad'i discourse (sababiyyah, sharitiyyah, mani'iyyah) contain iqtida' (requirement) implicitly, although not explicitly, because the result of these three is obligation and prohibition, which are among the types of iqtida'. Similarly, all causes, conditions, and preventers can be interpreted and included in implicit iqtida'. Therefore, no additional restriction is needed for wad'i hukm. The author (of the matn) went to the view that the truth is that the restriction 'aw al-wad'' should be added to the definition of hukm, because when two types of discourse are mentioned (taklifi and wad'i) and only one is mentioned, the other type should also be mentioned so that the definition is comprehensive. The author also said that including wad'i discourse in iqtida' or takhyir (i.e., in taklifi discourse) is not correct, because these two are different in meaning and are mutually exclusive, and including one mutually exclusive in another is not correct; rather, each must be mentioned independently. In some cases, the two imply each other, but that does not indicate their unity, e.g., the setting of the sun implies the obligation of prayer, but the two are different. So reflect. Commentary! The commentator Taftazani, in answering the third objection, made two groups of Ash'aris. The first group accepts the objection and adds the restriction 'aw al-wad''. For the second group, the narrator quotes two answers: first, they do not accept wad'i discourse as hukm at all; second, they accept it but say the restriction is not necessary, rather wad'i is included in implicit iqtida'. But Taftazani attributed this answer to the second group, which is wrong; rather, this answer is from another group. The reality is that there are three groups of Ash'aris responding to the third objection: (1) First group: they accepted the problem and added 'aw al-wad''. (2) Second group: they do not accept wad'i discourse as hukm at all and do not add 'aw al-wad''. (3) Third group: they accept wad'i as hukm but do not accept adding 'aw al-wad''; rather, they include wad'i in implicit iqtida' by making iqtida' inclusive of explicit and implicit. See the text of 'Allamah 'Adud al-Din in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Usul: 'Indeed the Ash'aris in this place are three groups: those who did not call wad'i hukm; those who called it hukm and added the restriction al-wad'; and those who called it hukm and included it [in iqtida'] by making iqtida' general, including explicit and implicit.' The author (of the matn) in his text did not mention the first group (who do not accept wad'i as hukm), declared the second group (who add 'aw al-wad'') as the chosen and correct, and rejected the third group (who include wad'i in iqtida'). But the commentator (Taftazani) combined the first group (who do not call wad'i hukm) and the third group (who call it hukm and include it in iqtida') into one group; this is a severe mistake. All the objections that Taftazani will later raise against the author are based on this misunderstanding; once this reality (that there are three groups) is revealed, those objections automatically disappear. And you know that this place has no justification at all. Taftazani raised objections against the author: that the author's statement (that 'aw al-wad'' should be added) is pure error and cannot be justified. First objection: The author's saying that the truth is to add 'aw al-wad'' so that wad'i hukm enters the definition is incorrect, because the opponent (the Ash'aris) is not ready to accept wad'i discourse as hukm; they only consider taklifi discourse as hukm. So for that, adding 'aw al-wad'' is not necessary; rather, it is necessary not to add it so that it remains outside and the definition prevents the entry of non-hukm. Answer! The answer to Taftazani's objection is: we have already clarified that there are three groups of Ash'aris: (1) a group that does not accept wad'i as hukm; the author did not mention this group in his text, nor did he refute or address it. The author only expressed his opinion regarding the two groups that accept wad'i as hukm: one adds 'aw al-wad'', the other does not and includes it in implicit iqtida'. The author said that the truth is to add 'aw al-wad'' and not include it in iqtida'. As for the opponent who does not accept wad'i as hukm, the author said nothing. Therefore, Taftazani's objection that the opponent does not accept it is invalid. Second objection: Even if the opponent (the Ash'aris) accepts wad'i discourse as hukm, they still do not feel the need for the restriction 'aw al-wad''; rather, they say it is included in the definition of hukm (without the restriction) because they interpret iqtida' in the definition of taklifi as comprehensive, covering both explicit and implicit, so it includes both taklifi and wad'i. Hence, adding 'aw al-wad'' is not necessary. As for the author's reason that the two are different in meaning and should be mentioned separately, the answer is: we accept that they are different in meaning, because taklifi is general and wad'i is specific, and general and specific are different in meaning. But their difference in meaning does not necessitate that they must be mentioned separately; rather, they can be included in each other by making iqtida' general, covering both explicit and implicit. The difference in meaning does not prevent their inclusion, just as general and specific are different in meaning but the specific is included in the general.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage presents a critical refinement of Taftazani's commentary on the definition of hukm (legal ruling) and whether it includes wad'i (posited) rulings. The author of the matn (likely Sadr al-Shariah) argues that the definition of hukm should include the phrase 'aw al-wad'' (or positing) to encompass wad'i rulings such as causes, conditions, and preventers. Taftazani objects, claiming that the Ash'aris either do not consider wad'i as hukm, or if they do, they include it within the iqtida' (requirement) of taklifi rulings. The author responds by clarifying that there are actually three Ash'ari positions, not two: (1) those who reject wad'i as hukm, (2) those who accept it and add the restriction, (3) those who accept it and include it in an expanded iqtida'. The author supports the second group and accuses Taftazani of conflating the first and third groups, thus rendering Taftazani's objections baseless. The key point is that the definition of hukm must be comprehensive and precise, and the Hanafi tradition typically adopts the position that 'aw al-wad'' is necessary to avoid ambiguity.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): Khitab (discourse) of the Lawgiver related to the acts of the accountable persons, comprising both taklifi and wad'i.
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): A ruling that posits something as a cause, condition, or preventer, such as the setting of the sun being a cause for the obligation of prayer.
اقتضاء (iqtida'): Requirement or demand, either explicit (sarih) in taklifi or implicit (dimni) in wad'i.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, how many groups of Ash'aris are there regarding the inclusion of wad'i hukm in the definition?
A) Two groups: those who add 'aw al-wad'' and those who don't.
B) Three groups: those who reject wad'i as hukm, those who add 'aw al-wad'', and those who include it in iqtida'.
C) Four groups: including those who consider wad'i as hukm but add no restriction.
D) Only one group: all Ash'aris agree on the definition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm explicitly includes wad'i rulings via 'aw al-wad'' to ensure comprehensiveness and avoid conflation of distinct categories.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Mutual Exclusivity of Hukm Taklifi and Hukm Wad'i
Debate on mutual exclusivity of hukm taklifi and wad'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish hukm taklifi from hukm wad'i based on their necessary consequences and state the Hanafi position that they are mutually exclusive (mutabayinan).

Core Idea
Hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are mutually exclusive because their necessary consequences differ—one entails command/prohibition, the other a relation between things.

In this passage, the author of Misk al-Malih defends the position of Sadr al-Shariah that hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are two distinct types that are mutually exclusive. The commentator al-Taftazani had argued that they are not mutually exclusive but only different in concept. The author rebuts by showing that their necessary consequences (lawaazim) are different, which proves the rulings themselves are mutually exclusive.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize that hukm is divided into taklifi (requiring or prohibiting action) and wad'i (establishing a relation between things).
This classification is fundamental in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the commentator's objection
Al-Taftazani claimed that the definitions of taklifi and wad'i are not mutually exclusive—there is 'no harm in their concepts' (la darar fi mafhumihima).
He argued they could overlap.
3
Analyze the author's rebuttal
The author points out that hukm wad'i necessarily involves a relation between two things, while hukm taklifi necessitates obligation or prohibition of an act. These consequences are different and mutually exclusive.
Mutual exclusivity of consequences proves mutual exclusivity of the rulings themselves.
4
Conclude the mutual exclusivity
Since the necessary consequences are mutually exclusive, the rulings themselves must be mutually exclusive (mutabayinan). Therefore, one cannot include the other.
This supports the Hanafi position that taklifi and wad'i are distinct types.

ہوتا ہے لہذا مصنف کا یہ قول کہ حق یہ ہے کہ او الوضع کی قید کا اضافہ کیا جائے ناحق ہے۔ جواب! مصنف کے قول کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ خطاب تکلیفی عام ہے خطاب وضعی کو بھی شامل ہے لیکن اولی یہ ہے کہ خطاب وضعی کو مستقلا ذکر کیا جائے کیونکہ دونوں مفہوم کے اعتبار سے متغایر ہیں، نیز جواب دوم) مقصود مصنف خطاب تکلیفی اور خطاب وضعی کے صرف مفہوم اور معنی کے تغایر کو بیان کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ مصنف ان دونوں کے تباین کو ثابت کرنا چاہتا ہے کہ یہ دونوں نوعان متباینان اور دو حقیقتان مختلفتان ہیں کیونکہ حکم وضعی کا لازم تعلق کئی بشئی آخر ہے اور کم تکلیفی کا یہ لازم نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کو وجوب فعل یا تحریم فعل لازم ہے اور یہ دونوں لازم آپس میں متغایر اور متباین ہیں اور تباین اللوازم دلالت کرتا ہے تباہین ملزومات پر اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ یفی اور خطاب وضعی متباینان ہیں اور ایک متباین کو دوسرے متبائین میں داخل کرنا درست نہیں تو شارح کا یہ کہنا فائی ضرر فی مفهومیھما غلط ہے کیونکہ ان میں تغایر مفہوم نہیں ہے بلکہ تباین مفہوم ہے اور یہ کہنا بھی درست نہیں فكيف يتحد مفهوم العام والخاص کیونکہ ان میں عموم خصوص نہیں بلکہ نسبت تباہین ہے ( کما عرفت انفا) على ان المفهوم یہاں سے شارح مصنف پر تیسرا اشکال کر رہے ہیں کہ مصنف نے خطاب وضعی کا مفہوم بیان کیا ہے ھو تعلق شئی بشئی آخر اس میں تسامح ( غلطی ) ہے کیونکہ خطاب وضعی تعلق شنی بشئی آخر نہیں بلکہ خطاب وضعی کی تعریف ہے الخطاب بتعلق شئی بشئی آخر تو مصنف نے خطاب کا لفظ ترک کر دیا ہے اس میں تسامح ہے کیونکہ خطاب وضعی نفس تعلق کا نام نہیں ہے بلکہ تعلق کے متعلق جو کہ خطاب ہے کا نام ہے فائھم۔ جواب! شارح کا یہ اشکال غلط ہے کیونکہ مقصود مصنف یہاں خطاب وضعی اور حکم وضعی کی تعریف اور معنی مطابقی کو بیان کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ مفہوم و معنی التزامی کو بیان کرنا ہے تا کہ حکم تکلیفی اور وضعی کا تباین واضح ہو جائے اور معنی التزامی تعلق شئی بشئی آخر ہی ہے لہذا مصنف پر تسامح کا الزام غلط ہے۔

وبعضهم عرف ذكر في بعض المختصرات غرض شارح تفتازانی اعتراض على المصنف! اعتراض یہ ہے کہ مصنف کا یہ قول کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے خطاب اللہ مطلق حکم کی تعریف کی ہے اور بعض نے اس کو حکم شرعی کی تعریف بنایا ہے درست نہیں ہے بلکہ تمام اشاعرہ کا اتفاق ہے کہ یہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے مصنف کو غلط نہی ہو گئی غلط نہیں اس وجہ سے ہوئی ہے کہ اشاعرہ کی بعض مختصرات ( مثلا مختصر ابن الحاجب ) میں یہ عبارت مذکور ہے الحکم خطاب اللہ الخ اس میں الحکم مطلق ہے مقید بقید الشرعی نہیں ہے اور اشاعرہ کی بہت سی کتب میں تصریح ہے الحکم الشرعی خطاب اللہ تعالیٰ مصنف نے عبارات کے اختلاف کو دیکھ کر و ہم کر لیا کہ اشاعرہ کا حکم کی تعریف میں اختلاف ہے بعض اشاعرہ خطاب اللہ کو مطلق حکم کی تعریف بناتے ہیں بعض حکم شرعی کی تعریف قرار دیتے ہیں حالانکہ یہ وہم غلط ہے کیونکہ جن بعض کتب میں الحکم مطلق ذکر کیا گیا ہے اس سے مراد بھی حکم شرعی ہے اور الحکم پر الف لام عهد خارجی ہے تو تمام اشاعرہ متفق ہیں کہ خطاب اللہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہے اور مصنف کا قیل

مسک الملیح
شرح التوضيح والتلويح

گیا ہے کہ بعض اشاعرہ نے خطاب اللہ کو مطلق حکم کی تعریف قرار دیا ہے فلا اشکال علی المصنف - قال المصنف الخ
وقيل کہنا غلط ہے۔ جواب! اعتراض تو ہم علی المصحف ساقط ہے کیونکہ پہلے بھی شرح منھاج کی عبارت نقل کر کے ثابت کیا

غرض شارح توضیح متن ہے! مصنف نے یہ فرمایا تھا کہ اگر خطاب اللہ مطلق حکم کی تعریف ہو تو پھر الشرعیہ کا معنی ما توقف علی الشرع ہوگا ماورد به الشرع نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اگر الشرعیہ کا معنی ماورد بہ الشرعیہ ہو تو یہ قید بے فائدہ اور مکرر مفید اور مخرج نہیں بنے گی کیونکہ اس سے پہلے جو حکم کا لفظ ہے اس کا معنی خطاب اللہ ہے اور یہ بھی ماورد به الشرع کے قبیل سے ہے پھر اگر الشرعیہ کی تعریف بھی ما ورد به الشرع کر دی جائے تو تکرار لازم آئے گا نیز اس سے وجوب ایمان وجوب تصدیق النبی بھی خارج نہیں ہونگے کیونکہ وہ بھی ماورد به الشرع کے قبیلہ میں سے ہیں اگر الشرعیہ کی تعریف ما يتوقف على الشرع کے ساتھ کی جائے تو یہ قید بے کار نہیں بلکہ با کار ہوگی ایک تو تکرار والا اشکال دفع ہو جائے گا نیز یہ قید مفید اور مخرج بنے گی اس سے وجوب ایمان وجوب تصدیق خارج ہو جائے گی کیونکہ وہ موقوف علی الشرع نہیں ہیں اور اگر خطاب اللہ الحکم الشرعی کی تعریف ہو تو پھر الشرعی کی تعریف ما ورد به الشرع ہوگی ( ما يتوقف على الشرع نہیں ہوگی ) اس لئے کہ اگر الشرعی جو کہ محدود اور معرف ہے اس کی تعریف ما توقف علی الشرع ہو تو محدود معرف خاص ہوگا اس سے وجوب ایمان وجوب تصدیق النبی خارج ہوں گے لیکن تعریف عام ہوگی کیونکہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف خطاب اللہ کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے وہ عام ہے سب کو شامل ہے۔ وجوب ایمان وجوب تصدیق النبی کو بھی شامل ہے تو حد محدود سے عام ہو جائے گی خلاصہ ایں کہ اگر خطاب اللہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہو تو شرعی بمعنی ماورد به الشروع ہوگا ما توقف علی الشرع نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اگر ما يتوقف على الشرع ہو تو تعريف عام ہوگی یعنی خطاب الله تعالى الخ وجوب ایمان وغیرہ سب کو شامل ہوگی لیکن معرف ( حکم شرعی ) خاص ہوگا لہذا در میں صورت معرف ( الشرعی) کا معنی ما ورد به الشرع ہوگا۔ قوله فالحكم على هذا اى على تقدير ان يكون! سے شارح تفتازانی هذا کا مشار الیہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ ہذا کا مشار الیہ ہے جب خطاب اللہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہو تو پھر اس تعریف میں مطلق حکم کی تعریف خطاب اللہ نہیں ہوگی بلکہ اسناد امرالی آخر ہوگی کیونکہ اگر مطلق حکم کی تعریف بھی خطاب اللہ ہو اور حکم شرعی کی تعریف بھی خطاب اللہ ہو تو پھر فقہ کی تعریف میں الشرعیہ کی قید لغو ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ جب حکم کا معنی بھی خطاب اللہ ہے یہ بھی ماورد به الشرع کے قبیل سے ہے اور آگے الشرعیہ کی تعریف بھی ماورد بہ الشرع ہوگی کیونکہ جب خطاب اللہ حکم شرعی کی تعریف ہو تو پھر الشرعیہ کا معنی ماورد بہ الشرع ہوتا ہے نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ الشرعیہ کی قید میں تکرار لازم آئے گا تکرار سے احتراز کرنے کیلئے حکم کا معنی اسناد امرالی آخر کیا جائے گا۔ فان قيل فيد خل الخ غرض اشکال و جواب ! اشکال یہ ہے کہ اگر شرعی کا معنی ما ورد به الشرع ہو تو وجوب ایمان وغیرہ بھی الاحکام الشرعیہ میں داخل ہو جائیں گے
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Misk al-Malih, Commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, pages 175-177. ... (full translation omitted due to length) ...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the author of Misk al-Malih addressing disputes between the commentator (Sharih, likely al-Taftazani) and the original author (Musannif, Sadr al-Shariah) of al-Tawdih. The first part debates whether hukm taklifi (prescriptive ruling) and hukm wad'i (declaratory ruling) are distinct categories with mutual exclusivity (tabayun) or merely different in concept (taghayur). The author argues they are mutually exclusive because their necessary consequences (lawaazim) differ: hukm wad'i entails a relation between two things, while hukm taklifi entails obligation or prohibition of an act. Therefore, one cannot be included within the other. The second part addresses an objection regarding the Ash'ari definition of hukm: some Ash'aris define hukm absolutely as 'khitab Allah', while others specify 'hukm shar'i'. The author clarifies that all Ash'aris intend the same—hukm shar'i—and apparent discrepancies in their texts are due to contextual differences (alif lam for 'ahd khariji). The third part explains the implications of defining 'shar'iyyah' as either 'ma warda bih al-shar'' (what the Lawgiver brought) or 'ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'' (what depends on the Lawgiver). If hukm is defined as khitab Allah absolutely, then 'shar'iyyah' must be the latter to avoid redundancy and to exclude pre-rational obligations like wujub iman. If hukm is defined specifically as hukm shar'i, then 'shar'iyyah' is the former, as the definition already limits it to shar'i matters. The commentator (Taftazani) elaborates on this nuance. All arguments are grounded in Hanafi usul methodology.

Key Terms
حكم تكليفي (hukm taklifi): A ruling that directly requires or prohibits action from the mukallaf, such as obligation or prohibition.
حكم وضعي (hukm wad'i): A ruling that establishes a relationship between something and something else, e.g., cause, condition, impediment.
لازم (lazim): Necessary consequence; what necessarily follows from a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what proves that hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are mutually exclusive?
A) Their definitions are different.
B) Their necessary consequences (lawaazim) are different and mutually exclusive.
C) The Qur'an separates them.
D) Ijma of the fuqaha.

Key Takeaway
Hukm taklifi and hukm wad'i are mutually exclusive because their necessary consequences (command/prohibition vs. relation) are mutually exclusive.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
10 min
Ash'ari Definition of Hukm and the Role of 'Shar'iyyah'
Resolution of apparent contradiction in Ash'ari definition of hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why all Ash'ari definitions of hukm refer to hukm shar'i and how the meaning of 'shar'iyyah' shifts depending on the definition of hukm.

Core Idea
Whether hukm is defined absolutely or as hukm shar'i, the term 'shar'iyyah' adapts to avoid redundancy and include/exclude pre-rational obligations.

This passage addresses an objection regarding the Ash'ari definition of hukm. Some Ash'ari texts define 'al-hukm' as 'khitab Allah' without qualification, leading to an apparent conflict. The author clarifies that the alif lam in 'al-hukm' is for 'ahd khariji, meaning it refers specifically to hukm shar'i. Consequently, the meaning of 'shar'iyyah' in the definition of fiqh changes: if hukm is defined absolutely, then 'shar'iyyah' must mean 'what depends on the Shariah' (ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar') to avoid redundancy and exclude pre-rational obligations like wujub iman. If hukm is already defined as shar'i, then 'shar'iyyah' means 'what the Shariah brought' (ma warda bih al-shar'). This nuance resolves apparent contradictions and maintains the Hanafi usul framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible definitions of hukm
Some Ash'ari texts define hukm absolutely as 'khitab Allah'; others define it as 'khitab Allah' specifically for shar'i rulings. Recognize that the alif lam in 'al-hukm' indicates a specific reference (ahd khariji) to hukm shar'i.
This resolves the apparent discrepancy.
2
Understand the implications for the definition of fiqh
Fiqh is defined as knowledge of the shar'i rulings. The term 'shar'iyyah' qualifies the rulings. Its meaning depends on whether hukm is defined absolutely or specifically.
The definition of fiqh must be consistent.
3
Analyze the two meanings of 'shar'iyyah'
If hukm is defined absolutely (khitab Allah), then 'shar'iyyah' cannot mean 'ma warda bih al-shar' because that would repeat the same concept; it must mean 'ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar' to include only those rulings that depend on Shariah (excluding pre-rational obligations). If hukm is already defined as shar'i, then 'shar'iyyah' can mean 'ma warda bih al-shar' because the definition already specifies.
This avoids redundancy and ensures proper scope.
4
Apply to example: wujub iman
The obligation to believe in God and His Prophet is a pre-rational obligation (wajib aqli). If 'shar'iyyah' means 'what the Shariah brought', then wujub iman would be included in fiqh. But fiqh only deals with Shariah-based obligations. Therefore, defining 'shar'iyyah' as 'what depends on Shariah' excludes wujub iman, aligning with Hanafi usul.
This shows the practical impact of the definition.
