کیا ہے اور جمع کا اطلاق ما فوق الا نہین پر ہوتا ہے جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ التي قد ظهر نزول الوحى بها الخ میں سے اگر ایک حکم یا دو کو معلوم کر نیا تو اس کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جائے گا اگر تین کو معلوم کر لیا تو اسے فقیہ کہا جائے گا جب کہ ملکہ استنباط ایک حکم یاد و کم جاننے کے وقت بھی تو حاصل ہے تو یہ مجیب تعریف ہے کہ محکم واحد یا حکمین مع ملكتة الاستنباط کے علم کو فقہ اور عالم کو قیہ نہیں کہیں گے اور صرف ایک حکم ثالث کے اضافہ کرنے کے ساتھ وہ فقیہ بن جائے گا : الجواب : شارح کا یہ اعتراض فرض محض پر مبنی ہے ورنہ ایک دو یا تیں احکام کے علم سے ملکہ استنباط حاصل نہیں ہو سکتا بلکہ ملکہ استنباط تو احکام جزئیہ کے ادراک مرة بعد مرة وبعد مدة طویلۃہ حاصل ہوتا ہے لہذا صرف ایک دوا حکام کے جاننے والے کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جائے گا وقيد نزول الوحي بالظهور احتراز عما اذا الخ غرض شارح نزول وحی کے ساتھ جو قید ظہور ذکر کی گئی تھی اس کا فائدہ بیان کرنا ہے وہ فائدہ: یہ ہے کہا اگر کسی حکم کے بارے میں نزولی وحی ہو چکا ہے لیکن ابھی تک وہ حکم ظاہر نہیں ہوا بایں طور کہ مجتہد فقیہ تک نہیں پہنچا تو فقیہ کیلئے اس کا علم ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ اگر فقیہ نے اس میں جتھاد کر لیا تو یہ اجتھاد صحیح ہوگا اس کے بعد جب اس حکم کی وحی مجتہد تک پہنچی اگر اس کا اجتھاد وحی کے موافق ہے تو فیھا اگر مخالف ہے تو اس کو اپنے قیاس اور اجتھاد سے رجوع کرنا واجب ہے قوله مع ملكة الاستنباط فرض شارح تشریح متن ہے سب سے پہلے تو شارخ نے یہ بتلایا کہ مع ظرف مقرون سے متعلق ہوکر العلم کے متعلق ہے یعنی وہ علم مقرون ہو ملکہ استنباط کے ساتھ پھر یہ بتلایا کہ الاستنباط پر جو الف لام ہے یہ مضاف الیہ کے عوض میں ہے اور مضاف الیہ کے بارے میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) مضاف الیہ فروع قیاسیہ ہوں اس صورت میں منھا کی ها ضمیر کا مرجع الاحکام ہونگے حاصل عبارت یہ ہوگا مع ملكة استنباط الفروع القياسيه من الاحكام المنصوصه (۲) دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ استنباط کا مضاف الیہ الاحکام ہو اس صورت میں منھا کی ضمیر کا مرجع ، ادلہ،
The Sharia rulings whose revelation has become apparent and upon which consensus has been reached, from their evidences, together with the faculty of correct deduction (istinbat). So fiqh is the name for knowing all those practical Sharia rulings with which the revelation of the wahy has become apparent, and the name for knowing all those rulings upon which consensus has been reached, along with the faculty of correct deduction. In short, fiqh is the knowledge of apparent textual rulings and consensus rulings together with the faculty of correct deduction. So 'al-mu'tabar' – the author is clarifying his definition: by 'all rulings' he means those textual rulings that exist in the time the faqih is present; they are all and complete, and knowledge of those revealed later is not necessary for the faqih at present. Thus the Companions were jurists in their time even though rulings were still being revealed and some were revealed later. As for when revelation has not appeared, it may not be known. The author explains the benefit of the word 'zahara' (appeared): until the appearance of the revelation, knowledge of it is not necessary for the faqih, rather it is not even possible, and the faqih's lack of knowledge before revelation does not harm his juristic capacity. 'And the Companions, due to their Arabicness, were knowledgeable.' From here the author explains the benefit of the condition 'with the faculty of correct deduction': to be a faqih, the faculty of deduction is necessary, because some Companions knew the textual rulings due to being Arabic speakers but did not have the faculty of deduction; they were not called jurists. Only those Companions who possessed deduction were called jurists. This shows that mere knowledge of textual rulings is not called fiqh, and the one who knows them is not called a faqih unless he has the faculty of deduction. Therefore the condition 'with the faculty of deduction' was added. 'And knowledge of consensus issues' – for the faqih, knowledge of consensus issues is also a condition, but the author clarifies that this condition is after the time of the Prophet and the Companions; in their time it was not a condition because revelation was ongoing and consensus did not exist. 'Not analogical issues' – the author explains that for the faqih, knowledge of textual and consensus issues is necessary, but knowledge of analogical issues is not necessary because if it were necessary, a vicious circle would result: analogical issues depend on the faqih's juristic capacity (since they are its result), so if the faqih's capacity depended on them, there would be a circle. Therefore, for the faqih, knowledge of analogical issues is not necessary; rather what is necessary is knowledge of textual and consensus issues along with the faculty of correct deduction. He explained the definition of correct deduction: correct deduction is that deduction which is accompanied by all its conditions. Misk al-Malih: Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. Sharh al-Talwih: His statement 'Rather it is knowledge' is an invented definition of fiqh. The commentator's purpose is to explain the text and criticize the author. First, this definition is invented and made-up, but Taftazani's criticism is not valid because all definitions are invented and conventional; no definition is sent down from heaven. Therefore the objection of invention is invalid. Rather, this invented definition has a good quality: although it is invented, it is precise for the objects of knowledge. The reason for its precision is four matters: (1) the word 'kull' (all), (2) the condition of the appearance of revelation, (3) the condition of the occurrence of consensus, (4) the condition of the faculty of deduction. And the restriction to all rulings: the benefit of the word 'kull' is that knowledge of some rulings is excluded; knowing some rulings is not called fiqh. But it indicates the commentator's purpose to criticize the author. The objection is that the author mentioned rulings in the plural in the definition of fiqh, and the plural applies to more than two, so if one knows one or two rulings from those whose revelation appeared etc., he will not be called a faqih; if he knows three, he will be called a faqih, even though the faculty of deduction may be present when knowing one or two. This leads to a defective definition: knowledge of one or two rulings with the faculty of deduction is not called fiqh, and adding just a third makes him a faqih. The response: the commentator's objection is based on a pure assumption; in reality, the faculty of deduction cannot be acquired from knowing one or two or three rulings; rather, the faculty of deduction is acquired by grasping partial rulings repeatedly over a long period. Therefore, one who knows only one or two rulings is not called a faqih. And the restriction of revelation by 'appearance' is to exclude cases where revelation has occurred but not appeared to the mujtahid; then knowledge of it is not necessary, and if the mujtahid exercises ijtihad, it is valid, but when the revelation reaches him, he must follow it. His statement 'with the faculty of deduction' – the commentator is explaining the text. First, he said that 'ma'a' (with) is related to 'ilm' (knowledge) as a circumstantial qualifier, meaning that knowledge is accompanied by the faculty of deduction. Then he said that the definite article on 'al-istinbat' is in place of the constructive genitive, and there are two possibilities for the constructive genitive: (1) the constructive genitive is 'furū' qiyāsiyya' (analogical branches); then the reference of 'minhā' is the rulings; the meaning becomes 'with the faculty of deducing analogical branches from textual rulings'. (2) The second possibility is that the constructive genitive is 'al-ahkām' (the rulings); then the reference of 'minhā' is the evidences.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of fiqh as presented in the text (al-Tawdih) and the critical response of Taftazani (in al-Talwih). The author defines fiqh as knowledge of Sharia rulings that have been revealed and on which consensus has been established, along with the faculty (malaka) of sound istinbat (deduction). The commentary breaks down each condition. First, the word 'kull' (all) specifies that a faqih must know the entire body of revealed rulings of his era, not future ones, as was the case with the Companions. Second, 'zuhūr al-wahy' (appearance of revelation) means the faqih is only responsible for rulings that have reached him; hidden revelations do not affect his status. Third, the condition of consensus is relevant only after the era of revelation. Fourth, the 'malaka' (faculty) distinguishes a mere transmitter from a true faqih, as some Companions knew Arabic and rulings but lacked derivation ability. Taftazani objects that the definition is 'invented' and that the plural 'ahkam' creates a problem: if knowing one ruling with the faculty is not enough, then adding a third magically makes one a faqih. The commentary refutes this by arguing that the faculty cannot be attained from just a few rulings; it requires long practice. It also explains the grammatical structure of 'ma'a malakat al-istinbat' and the two interpretations of the idafa. The overall conclusion is that fiqh requires comprehensive knowledge of revealed and consensus rulings combined with a deep-rooted ability to derive new rulings.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of Sharia rulings that have been revealed and upon which consensus exists, along with the faculty of correct derivation.
ملكة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): A stable faculty in the soul enabling the derivation of rulings from their evidences with all conditions.
الاجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah after the Prophet's era on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in this passage, what is the minimum requirement for a person to be called a faqih?
A) Knowing at least three revealed rulings with the faculty of deduction.
B) Knowing all revealed rulings of his era and consensus rulings, with the faculty of correct deduction.
C) Knowing any number of rulings without the faculty of deduction.
D) Knowing only Quranic verses without hadith.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is not just knowledge of Sharia rulings but also includes a stable faculty (malaka) for deriving new rulings, which is developed over time.
